Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then make him enter or bathe until the flesh is somewhat stiff, and then make him enter or lie down, and the pain will go away entirely and be healed
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And as for wounds that no one must use the fire cautery on until after the evacuation of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And thus Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with vinegar, if it helps with moisture; and it must be done cautiously in parts.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb and the great toe and the other which is called the fossicle
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking vinegar of chivers dry, and wet it with fire until it is charred, and put it on the lint, and leave it until it is stained; and do this again and do not stop doing this until you think by sense that it has gone down to the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "chiver cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes from the back, or from sitting or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things of cold expanding matter, none of these symptoms is worth cautery, save for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is free from foul pills or other similar things, that we make on his back, there or where the pain is, three lines signed with a needle, and in a fourth line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small swelling, and its signs are that when it swells it hurts the loin and causes fear; and you find it behind the lower spine on the back and its appearance comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize at the cautery of this circle according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery touches some part of the spine excessively.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the cautery has gone too deep into the spine, two or three lines from the point where it pricked, keep the points close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound as described above, keep the limb steady until it is healed, and take care that you do not cause any damage to the nerves in haste
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain comes from a piece that is called "podagre" properly, and when the cause is cold and treated by medicines, it cannot be cured; if it is cured by cautery in part: make the mouth of the cautery enter the joint at the point of pain, and let the cautery be of the olive kind according to this fashion:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need to prick on the face of the bone, if you are using the whole cautery, call it "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there are pains that come up to the knees and other joints, and this often occurs, if you are doing cautery on each knee three times or four on each part, with the olive oil cautery; and if you must do more, do more, but do not hold your hand too tight until the piece of meat is cooked through
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are as high as the hands, if you prick twice at the base of the thumb; and if there is no more pain at the two ends, if you prick at the wrist and at the nail of the hand; and if the pains come down to the buttocks or down to the heels, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient drink a potion and prescribe medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him drink a potion and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oes does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell, they will not aid.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a fracture approaches the shoulder, and the ball comes loose as new, if you wish to cure it, do not break off the limb; and do use things that leave the belly open, so that the pain may go down from the belly; afterwards let him sit on his buttocks between your hands, and command him to hold his arm tight until the bone is healed, and keep it firm at your sides, and mark on the skin above the collarbone the extent of the fracture, and do all that is like half a circle below the bone. Then withdraw the cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as he is limp and sweats, he feels sensations.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then loosen the bowels at their place; and hold his hand so that they do not return backwards; and keep the patient warm, and put a cushion under his chest and another under his hand; then place the cautery on the sign at the top of the hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you have reached the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware prudently that the bowel does not slip while you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And nails that until you reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be known that the cautery of small vessels must be subtle in measure and of great men also great in measure; after three days cure the limb from the burn until the scab is bony; after cure other ointments until they are healed; and keep the patient forty days on his back until the wound is well healed; and it must be known that its bruises must be long-lasting, so that the swelling does not appear when he moves to the bedroom.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wishes to rise, he must have a well-made support and carry it for forty days; and have good rest, that he works little and takes care to avoid too great indulgence in drink and eating, and too great haste; and when he has done this teaching, he will be entirely healed
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall speak of the treatment of the fistula in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the treatment of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When they come out in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, if you make the burn of the cautery return to its quantity, and be three parts of the fourth; treat it as we have said; neither of the old ones have said that it should be burned with the cautery at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the limb with a line above the fistula and one below, and hold your hand firmly with all your might over the cautery clamp
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	...there is no greater pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, or in the hip or the flank, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medical treatment is not of avail, then it is necessary to cauterize with the cautery which is called “points,” and cauterize according to the length of the limb and its smallness and frailty and virtue and location of torsions and pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sane after the first cautery, it is well; if not, repeat the cautery on that one, for it is customary that it must burn the part that is nearest, in order that you may make the cauteries as long as the patient is sane.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from injury or ailment, and the pain persists for a long time, medical treatment is of no avail; therefore, it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery known as the "poins," or with a cautery according to the length of the limb, its smallness and weakness, its toughness and its tortures, and its pain. If successful in the first cautery, well and good; if not, repeat the procedure once more for it is customary to effect the cauteries as close to the diseased part as possible, so that the pain is relieved while the disease is still present.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease never helps itself by cautery, and indeed the same illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see it being cauterized? Take warning if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, do not linger, and do not doubt that corruption does not spread throughout the whole illness; then make five cauteries on the head: one on the new head, and one towards the front at the end of the beard; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the cheek; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the scabs are forced out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	If the mess is scattered everywhere; and it appears manifestly, if you must indeed cauterize with these cauteries which we have spoken of or chief, namely the cautery in some places you desire not to, and two cauteries on the armpits, and three on the spine of the neck, and one great on the hip and one other from below, and two on the two scapulae, and two on the flanks, and two on the tendons of the wrist and elbow, and one on almost every joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; take heed of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and in no way perform cautery on the bone of the heel or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And so it is that the more he makes the cautery, the more he renders help, and it benefits him; and so it is that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as he would from the pain of an abscess, because the flesh is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the cautery must be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you see in the handling of the instruments.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the wound with flour of wheat sometimes with honey and other cures until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured with medicines and oils and patches, and it is not healed, then you must make cauteries on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and that the cauteries are thrust into the thickness of the flesh; then cure with ointments until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never is the fire cautery done with hand and foot and back, at the issue of nerves that move the limb, and thus if the bone is fractured it swells; and in no way should anything intervene between them unless they are skilled in the members and the issues of the moving nerves around the bone.
de albaras	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not entirely healed, then you must make cauteries on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either make the cauteries a little deeper than the depth of the nerve that moves the limb; then cure with ointments until it is healed. And never make a cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the exit of a nerve that moves the limb, and so if it is bony the swelling will remain. And in no way should anything be interposed that does not know the limbs and the exits of the moving nerves from the bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicine is of no avail, then you must make a cautery with a needle a little deep, according to the depth of the tissue, until the swelling is bony and has changed color; then cure with flour of times, lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and alum, a part of each; mix them all together, and bind with a bandage, and keep it in place until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, if you burn it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all these people say that it is done with the middle of the boil; and all these things do not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it does not happen; and the right thing is to burn around the boil, with the cautery which is called the circle, as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an ailment called "adubelati" and it is late in healing or due to excessive swelling or excessive blood in the wound when it is decrepit (that is, too much time has passed) and there is little blood, or due to tension; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; after that, leave it be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turning pale with all the cautery, if it is hot, take away the cautery for a moment: thus is the shape
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has perceived the heat, and be such cauteries that the patient feels the fire diminishing in part as the wound progresses.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After that, cure as long as it remains perfectly healthy
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another disease that is called "corrodens" exists, and is nothing other than a weakening of the limb, for it causes the limbs to become soft as dry bones.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the limb which can suffer from fire cautery, then burn the nails of the little and great toes cautiously, according to what the limb or the disease demands; after cauterizing all parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains except the bone itself.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized parts a cloth soaked in oil until the eschar becomes dry like burnt leather, and all the corruption
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Then the treatment of these wounds that leave scars.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days the hairs do not grow back, it is well; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This disease is never cured by medical treatment alone; but indeed, the fire cautery is of greater help, as I have already said in the preceding section. Take as much as you need of it.</start_of_turn>
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the wounds that come from the heel to the toe.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times we have seen that when the feet swell up due to a wound, a disease called "clos" occurs, which is a large and painful swelling.</start_of_turn
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	The cautery for this disease is done in two ways.</start_of_turn
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and warm water cautery.</start_of_turn
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	If thou art to cauter with fire, I command thee to cauter as with a needle of wool, and make it of strong iron of the measure that it may penetrate the root of all parts, and that there be subtle margins; then put all about the root, and press thy hand round about the root until it comes to the front of the root; and leave it there for three days until it begins to fester; then make an embalmment of wild mallow bruised with oil, and leave the embalmment upon all night, and close the wound firmly and it shall be drawn out of its root.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	If they are converted by boils of foul matter, and often happen in hands and feet, if you must bring them near, apply a hot cautery; for it is in part a remedy. Then leave it alone, and it will discharge all its roots.

li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide. quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.

Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This text is not included in the requested translation, as it is not provided in the input.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that in all diseases where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or apply burning medicine, we must inquire into the omens, causes, instruments, and shapes of the cauteries; and in this chapter we will speak of the chief matters that we have found to be lighter in this way than in others.</start_of_turn>

Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	For if it is not firmly held, if you do not hold it tightly without doubt in all things.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is over the temple until the second incision; and squeeze all the marrow which is between the two incisions to the very surface of the bone, then do the rest of the wound until the other second, and then remove this thumb and index finger.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first fissure the instrument which is called the "cultellaire", and is very well cut on one side, and on the other is smooth, do not cut deeply, and this is its form:

And cut all the blood vessels that go down from the head as long as the incision is continuous until it reaches the shoulder, and then do the same in the middle of the fracture until the other side; then drain the blood equally, and express the limb for the blood taken; then put in the wound a patch of cotton wool, and cover with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and wool, and keep that the edges of the wound do not move; and after three days remove the dressing, and mix a great quantity of cold water, then cure the wound with basilic ointment with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	because of repeated swelling
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste. de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes swelling of the ears is among these things: grains, or pus, or stone or other foreign bodies like iron; or seeds, like peas, beans, or beans; or fluid-filled things like urine and saliva or other things.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it hurts in the ear, bone or other thing that does not fit into the ear, do not put it in, but put the ear on the sole of the foot

Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times blood comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, order extraction as fine needles, for this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by itself, that is good; if not, extract it with a fine needle of double curvature; and if it does not come out even with that, make an injection of ointment and cut off the top of the injection or break the ear very much, and stamp what is around the injection of ointment if it comes out and cannot enter with the needle; then the pain will cease, for often it comes out by itself as we have said; and if it does not come out in part, take hold of the ear and put on no instrument that can cause injury, and put a little cloth over; then press the hold on the stone or whatever it is, and the pain will cease.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things fail, if you are in haste to make an incision at the ear root or at the base of the jaw, and spasm, do as follows: make the first incision at the front of the head, and drain blood in accordance with its quantity. Then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fatty or bony prominence. Make the incision as wide as a crescent, until you reach the bone, and remove the pus promptly from your mouth. Continue the treatment until the wound is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is a grain that is ensnared and swells, administer extraction; if it cannot be extruded, administer a sponge held tightly according to this form:

de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some hole in their ear; and the same thing happens at home through wound bursting or earwax being blocked in the ear, for these bursts never happen without leaving a mark on the ear, if one does not see; and never happens without a certain degree of loss of hearing, which one sees very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When these bursts happen without being seen, they are a sign of serious illness in many cases, and in this case one sees that you put the painful ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opilation apparent, if the swelling has completely disappeared, this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee. Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.

de la gresle	De la gresle.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come out of paper things that seem greasy in their form and in their hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "granule", and is an assembly of large moisture in the substance of the wound; the work is like this: take care that if the granuloma swells up from one side and the other, it is a light matter to know; then make the opening wide, then slightly burn the surrounding part, then take hold of the wound, and close.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not perceive enough sense to perceive the wound, if it does not grieve the patient; and if the wound is great, if the contents have a bulge, and the treatment is as long as it takes until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, because the wound itself restores quickly and heals quickly.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the granulin descends downwards towards the ear towards the upper part, reverse the wound, and bring the granulin to a few pinches; grasp and press from one side to the other; and if the wound is stripped by the incision, it will grieve nothing; and when the wound is closed, leave the dirty oil, and cure the limb of that which leaves a scar as long as the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the blood
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	The oily exudate is enclosed in papers of paper which are softened by heat; this happens more often in women than in men, and causes great swelling at their eyes, and they weep continuously; and because of this they keep their eyes shut and lie sleeping, and their papers are softened by their tears which swell up and appear covered in the oily exudate which emerges in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb towards your chest and feel the exudate between the shoulder blades,

des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like tissues grow hair-like bristles other than their natural state, and are thickened, if they irritate the eyes, they cause various diseases such as tears, and softening of the paper-like tissues and mucus, as well as the destruction of the hairs; and the cure for this is in three ways: either by whole-body cautery with fire, or by means of water medicine as I have said, or by incision and stitching or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient’s hand over your left hand; if the paper changes, that is good; if not, if there is an awl with a single thread at the root of the hair; whether you cut the edge of the paper or the hair sprouts from these hairs, take a single thread from the root of the hair to the tip of the paper, and stretch it out; then pull out the hair from the root, from the root of the bristles to the tip of the nail; then draw out the single thread, and put on the paper a small patch of cotton and bandage, and mark on the paper a sign like the mark of a thrush, and know that the sign must be in accordance with the quantity of the paper that you see being lifted that is required for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it comes to the vein above the ankle, if the cure of closing blood vessels is too great while it is still sane.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold together that which is above with small forces equally following the shape that is there.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the teeth firmly, and the matter is not equal, take a needle or two and pass a thread through the figure; and pass another thread loosely around the great loop, and the second thread loosely around the little loop, and join the two threads together evenly; then hold your hand evenly, and hold all the skin around which you have signed, as we have recounted; and join the two layers of the wound together by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and similar soothing dressings. Never again shall the hair of the papillae be converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard and the hair inwards as I have said, then make four incisions by art, and four fine threads as long as the beard and the diameter of a hazelnut; and put in four hairs or hold the threads. Then assemble the one and the other firmly on that which rests on the oil of the beard; strain the four incisions from the four parts forming; and leave it so for several days, and the skin which has been strained will become pale and wrinkled and will swell, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the boil has great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is closed and the papillae are withdrawn, they will not prick again; and this is the form of two nails you shall make according to this figure and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a fine needle, and there is inside it a thread of silk fine and subtle; then assemble the hairs and do not knot one with the other subtly, and let the length of the thread be as long as a palm; then command in the chase another thread subtle of silk briefly, and do not knot the chief with the thread; then put the patient's chief in your hand; and let go of the sun if the work is clarified, for it is a subtle and light work, then withdraw the needle at all the chase in the root of the hair which grows naturally; then pull out the hair until it breaks at the root as much as you pull out naturally; then draw out the hand as much as the vein escapes at all the chase in the palm with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have commanded, until the chase vein comes out from under and you see it through the vision of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair comes back to its place and the burden is gone.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the putrefaction comes to the boil, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there comes from the wound, or from the ulcer or the cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of working in this is that you close the wound, dry the flesh, put in lint, and leave it until it is healed; and do not do anything but use things that dry and restrain
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, if the disease comes back worse than before; but there are things that soften, such as fennel; and alum or salt and poppyseed be boiled in any oil, and it covers a bandage, and treats this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the form it had before; and this work that we have said is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from the form it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the fire that comes from the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called saxacrati in reality is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	This disease which is called saxacrati in reality is natural and accidental. The cause comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and things similar; and the way of the disease is that if you take an awl, because it has two folds, and the handle in the flesh, and it pierces the left tear duct so that the vein bursts through two fingers of the flesh; then the flesh above is raised up to the awl, and the handle has one large spathe.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the mark of the awl comes back as it should, that is good; if not, take a saw and put it into the wound, and turn the bone, and make two incisions or break two bones within the bone; and if two fingers of the two incisions which you have made are cut, or if you make one angle so that when they are reunited, the mark should be as if it were the letter that has not "two knees"; then hold that bone according to the quantity of its cost and its weight, of that which sustains the bone, then join the two broken parts with a thread of silk; then cure with what we have said of the mollifying medicines and patches, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the ailment comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is known that there is hair loss from papery substances, and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be carried out according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know everything better than I do concerning the return of the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him and the instruments in more numerous positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	If the ailment comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if it is known that there is hair loss from papery substances, and as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be carried out according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know everything better than I do concerning the return of the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him and the instruments in more numerous positions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stiffness arises at home in part as the limb above is soothed with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural works, if it is known that the bone has been fractured, then it must be bled from the point of a scraper from below the bone, and held up high; and the edges must be bound as tightly as possible, without causing excessive pain, for the patient cannot endure too much pain or excessive bleeding; and the incision, which you have made, must be slight, so that the limb returns to its natural shape; and all that is assembled must be thoroughly cleansed, and no longer washed in salted water, but with fresh water, and oil; and between the bone and the oil put a bandage of lint, and cover the oil with coarse wool in abundance; and after that apply a support as much as is necessary until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The fennel oil has two kinds: one is nervous and somewhat dark like pitch, and the other is not nervous but is like pale moisture that solidifies when touched by iron and becomes black like soot; both of them begin to soften towards the great marrow, and grow so much that they cover the whole cavity and the brightness and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And as for the incision, if the patient places his head in its right place, then hold the eyes; then grasp the hair with your hand, then take a needle and make a small incision at the root of the hair; insert one hair of a horse, or of a sheep, or of a bull, and a strong thread; double the point of the needle once and pass the needle through the hair, and grasp the hair with the thread and pull it out, and with all the hair surrounding the root that surrounds the nail and the hair to the root, then cut away all the superfluous tissue until only a little bit of the natural oil remains; and if there is no other discharge from the incision, do not extend the incision alone, but with the thread as we have said; then stretch out the surrounding tissue as much as possible.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the spatula does not touch the fatty tissue and breaks it, and that the needle is not perceived; and after the incision pour oil a little bit of bruised salve, and apply a bandage, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread does not go in, many times this semblance of a nail of medicine is cured; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you pour oil on the patient, and take the spatula lightly according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail gradually, and if you see that it has diminished point and the wound is pressing, if you distill from your mouth into the oil bandage make of alum and red salve, and bruise the salve, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other operation according to this same operation, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk first and cure the abscess thoroughly while it is sound, then repeat the work as before, while it is sound.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	If there appears in the oil at night a piece of soft tissue that causes great swelling, if you suspend it on an onion and cut off a part and not all, that blood does not arise; then distill in the red oil of colera which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the plumule.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But always know that you should temper the treatment with a weak oil of natural origin; and by chance, in the work of iron; and do not move your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	Des voines des eulz.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The veins are red which are covered with oil, and endure the gaze of the fire and burn the oil entirely every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The physician must first observe that the oil is indeed on the veins, for if it is not, the pain is fierce, and there is no other disease more fierce than this; therefore the physician must do this in parts: instruct the patient to place his head in his health, then suspend the veins all around as he deems fit, and let the incisions be as subtle as possible in this fashion.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	Red veins covered with oil, tolerate the gaze of the eye and expel the oil throughout the days. The surgeon must therefore be the first to notice if the oil is strong; for there is no other disease more violent than a wound; therefore the surgeon should act immediately: instruct the patient to put his head in a normal position, then suspend those veins to the utmost extent of his skill, and do so discreetly in the following manner:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Red veins covered with oil, tolerate the gaze of the eye and expel the oil throughout the days. The surgeon must therefore be the first to notice if the oil is strong; for there is no other disease more violent than a wound; therefore the surgeon should act immediately: instruct the patient to put his head in a normal position, then suspend those veins to the utmost extent of his skill, and do so discreetly in the following manner: discreetly suspend those veins without causing any pain, and let the blood drain out afterwards; do this work at midday when the sun is shining, and be wary of any spasms.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot bear all this in that hour, make an ointment from oil and soothing things to soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pain is appeased and the swelling has subsided; then repeat according to this manner until you are well; this is the way of strength.
de la fistule de l’oil	And if you cannot bear all this in that hour, make an ointment from oil and soothing things to soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pain is appeased and the swelling has subsided; then repeat according to this manner until you are well; this is the way of strength.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and medicine with burning water, as I have said before, and it is not completely healed, if there is still something remaining on the incision, leave it in place and drain all the moisture from it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone breaks, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the limb has all the elements to be whole; it is called an "aspre chief," and be made of burnt ivory, that is, a broken bone, and be pointed out as with a lime as when it is in this form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the limb the broken bone, then twist it between your two hands, and press your hand until you feel that the corruption is reset; do this never, then restore the limb of exiccative medicines.</start_of_turn>
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the limb is dislocated, and the char is not born, and the flesh of the limb is dislocated, and remains so for XL days, and does not heal and is not closed, and the patient does not recover, even if he be well; if this is not the case, if there is no other remedy except to open the fistula again by force, and by sharp medicines, and when it has been opened as much as is necessary, take hold of the limb at three angles, and the fistula should be reduced to its natural position as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place your thumb on the bone below the lump, and wipe your hand with oil; then pull the thread all the way through until it breaks the bone and the patient feels it through the skin where the thumb has been resting; and when the thread has gone in, restore the dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the thread comes out and becomes firm, if there is matter in the thumb; if it is less serious for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the elbow, and move your hand away from the oil immediately, then pull the limb back until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes from under his arm if he keeps his hand on his elbow.  Then restore the dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the wound heals and the limb endures, if there is still matter in the elbow; if it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the limb opens all at once, and there is no displacement of the navel, no swelling, if you must bind the patient; then loosen it, and put on a bandage or dressing in a circular fashion to suck out the wound, then put on oil.i. with acaice and aloe and incense and beeswax, and then strain the oil, and replace it with lint and cloth; and keep the cloth in place if you take cloth enough soft, and double bandage in three layers, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the wound has in it; then strain it by pressing down with a stiff bandage, and reapply the dressing to suck out the wound in a circular fashion; then tie the dressing and leave the oil strained for a night, and if the wound has softened, if you must strain it out; then tie the limb up after the night and the morning, and if you see the oil returning, that is good; if not; continue the dressing and the cloth and the limb and the dressing until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dou derrompement de toile uvee.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, then open the joint, and if there are papers within like grains of resin, leave them; for it is expected to see them. If you see them covered, the work is like biting an awl at the root of the lower part until below the middle, then insert another awl or there is a double thread of the lower part; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl as it lies. Then grasp the double thread and bind the upper part of the limb firmly, then pull out the awl and put on lint soaked in oil in abundance; and leave it until the thread is severed with the limb, then cure the oil of comforting things until the wound is healed; and never is the wound restricted by the limb that is under tension by a circle of silk, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has great appearance, if you pierce at the soft cartilage which comes from the middle of the oil, and correct the moist vapor and bring down the wound, and put them together; then pull out the awl until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	The disease called "alcunnati" is not fierce but dull, which is put together in oil, resembling descending ice, and it is not actually ice; and the way this disease appears is that you make the patient sit on a comfortable and upright chair, and take hold of the chief between your hands two parts, and move it until you see the dullness coming down to your eyes; then either bind it tightly and do not remove the light, or break the light and see the patient do the same; and if it does not descend, it is like ice, and if it descends gradually as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If thou seest the patient sitting between thy hands, then take the sponge and place it upon the corn of the eye I by the course of the conjunctiva with the corn of the eye and the brow, until the eye is released; and when it is out, distill into the hot oil mixed with honey, or into vinegar or fenugreek boiled with honey, then let it be cured of some other remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the belly of the oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the signs of worms in the division, and what it is proper to do; if in their work they please the health.
