Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must make the patient sit between your hands crossed, and take away the light from the sun, and put on the oily unguent and tighten the mouth very firmly; then take the thumb of your left hand if the eye is left, or your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called the “almagda,” or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument below the brow by the thickness of a nail at the part where the lesser tear meets the greater tear, and pull out the instrument which is called the “almagda” usefully, and restore your hand until it pierces in the tear, and feel that the “almagda” comes to the empty thing; and it is the measure of the almagda that is at the height of the measure of the space from the plum of the nail to the end of the black. And that is the brow of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corn of the eye, then put the instrument until it is almost level or the water is, and then press the thumb away from the way after the other.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels pain now, if he sees the patient in front of him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a little rest, if he feels pain again, if he sees the patient in front of him and the instrument in his oil, grasp the instrument with force and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, grasp the thumb and index finger lightly around the hand towards the thumb and index finger; and then reintroduce the thumb into the oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force the oil soaked with wool or cloth soaked in rose oil and in abundance of eggs, and bind with the pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are of our age, put on wool broth with abundance of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda does not enter the oil because there are too many hairs in the way, since this is the shape of the instrument:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva slightly, and do not go too deeply, but make the limb limp, then put the thumb back in place; as we have said. And at the end of the work appears to the patient the bearer of the wound, who sleeps on his back in the dark; and be careful of all movements, and take gentle food, and do not move his head forward or backward, and bind according to his disposition until the seventh day; then take him out of this house to the same dark place, and ask him to look at something, and do not let him see anything, and then put his hand back in the same place as before. Do not do this at the beginning of the treatment or after the incision now, but do make sure that you feed him, for he has become very hungry
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Leave the hairs long and even, and if you prick them at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. For in this work, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die. When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury. Leave the hairs long and even, and if you prick them at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. For in this work, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go from the house to the field, and in such cases convert; and towels that no disciple must interfere with in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Yrach region who told us that in their peace they used to do an ointment with honey that when it was applied to the wound, the pain would subside; however, we have never seen or heard of such a thing in our land or in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing for us.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of an almond, for he who does not know them will not recognize them; and be of barley properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their tops are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a goosefoot.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the wrist.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are born or fall diverse hairs, that which seem like scorpions in their mouths; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with blood-red color, or hair of sulfur color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	When these hairs are of sulfur and not entangled, it is sufficient that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; cover their nose, and throw the urine on those hairs, and drive them away; for thus you will support the subtle gut from the sharp part until you are certain that the hair is entirely dry.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the opening has all its instruments lightly held, if nothing is left; and if without you snoring, or incision close to the eye, if the escape is like it should be; and if it is malignant incisions, hasten and cauterize as much as you can until it is stained and the hair is burned over, then spit or do not spit easily, but with pain or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it does not happen that the urine comes, and moisture comes up to the palate, be sure that it is healthy; and if moisture does not cease if it should, be sure that there is new hair in the bone below, for the flesh does not come out whole: therefore you must drink a large thread of linen, and grasp it with your hands, and give it between each nipple an inch or less; and put the patient’s head on the thread at the bottom, and treat it until it comes out through the nipple; and many times do the children do this, and it is a light matter for him who has seen it done; then hold the chief which comes out through the nipple to one hand, and the other chief which comes out through the mouth to the other hand, and grasp one after the other while sitting as we are or as we have.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of gold, like a large lamp, if like a sponge; and guide it thus; and if you see, make a close bundle, and make the instruments flat to purge the chief; and have one hand on the chief to hold it when we burn oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the wrist.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the root of the arm a disease which is called “telul,” and it grows and becomes great at once, so that it appears like a thing to behold; and because of this it is expedient that you should commence to apply the cautery or burning medicine at the outset, and break the bone afterwards; and if you delay in covering it when it is great, if you take warning when it is hard, of foul discharge, of bad sense: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a swollen abscess, for when you touch it once, there results great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of foul discharge, you can see that you can cover it all, if you drain the patient and cover it with oil, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the arm is cut and bound
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do as such while you know that they [the boils] have not corrupted the hair, then draw the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam, and put it back in place as before; do this for three days or more, until the abscess has corroded all that remains of the hair; and then put on or remove a cautery sponge for a few days until it is healed, and if there is need for sedatives, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, from which we distill the oils and medicines or not.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not happen in any way, if you observe that the wound is fresh throughout its entirety; then join the two layers to a rib, and cure until it is healed. If the layers are already separated from one side and the other, if you can, hold all the parts together until they bleed, then reassemble the two layers to a rib, and strain, and sprinkle over it powdered dragon’s blood, and incense. Place upon the powders a piece of packing of great or other solid dressing, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, then cure until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch is that you reassemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said in the costure of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the edges of the wound
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home on the hands there are dense layers of skin, sometimes like grains of wheat, smaller and larger; therefore it is likely that you will tear the skin and make incisions on each little hair, and grasp them with tweezers and pull them out at the root; then employ the paste after the incision of the little carbuncle, until it is no longer stained; and then remove the paste easily, and cure the limb of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the teeth of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times comes upon the gums the white teeth which are called 'albuly'; if you support them, grasp the root and pull out the socket or the blood; then take out the little carbuncle with the vitriole burn or other astringent and drying powders; and if the tooth comes out after the incision, and this happens often, if you grasp it a second time and burn it; if it does not come out after the burn; this is the form of the instruments to cover it
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Once are gathered at the root of the tooth, within the mouth between the gums, teeth that are white and rough; and never are the teeth black and yellow and soft, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and are the teeth biting; if it is that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulder be in your chest, and open the teeth or the gums open, until there remains nothing; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other spots, as long as they are whole; and if one has what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, if he must repeat the second and third time, until you have done everything; and the teeth that have mixed with various forms of instruments to repair, according to what the work shows, for the raisers of the teeth that you must drive out have other forms than those with which you must drive between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you visible.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you do not leave it too long to treat it as much as you wish, for this must not be done carelessly; for it is a high-quality material so therefore we have no excuse for omitting to drive it out
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to suffer, if you are certain that it is necessary, you must be certain that he will endure it.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient feels pain, and it is cured either because it is already absent or because it has become accustomed; and every time the pain does not depart despite this, as long as the patient remains alive, for we have already wished to make them suffer; and when you are well certain that he will endure it, if you can, hold his hand firmly to all sides; then pull the limb strongly from the root and hold firmly in place at the first and second joints, until they are well dislocated; then confirm them well. Be sure that the patient’s limb is completely still between your thighs, and hold it firmly if it does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, stretch the tooth outwards towards the cheek, and if it does not yield, take none of these instruments and hold it loosely within the cheek, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if it is grasped and softened, if you can, cover it with bandages, or if you have pierced it; and if you strain it cautiously, do not break it while straining; and must keep your mouth moist over the gum to soften the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first time.</start_of_turn
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware that you do not do like the ignorant layman, who break their bones at every opportunity without any reason, and do not listen to what we have told them; but they bring about their own downfall through the root of great pain, or the fracture itself, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply a piece of vitriol sponge; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it.</start_of_turn
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, when they are mute at first, whether with long points and broad handles, that they do not double much when you draw the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great limbs if they do not bend much when you draw, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so as to hold them in place.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains fixed at the back, if you must take out the moist cotton swab that is in the ear, do it with forceps or your fingers.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the limb is softened, since the nails appear like barley corn, make them as thin as can be made with a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to withstand all these tensions, if you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument which is called “althali,” which is to say tweezers, for this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and firm, lest it break my skin, and if the root jumps by this, that is good; if not, aid it with all your instruments, for these shapes will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has teeth, for this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, whose form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, whose form is as follows: let this instrument be strong enough not to break, and its handles like those of other instruments for teeth; and there are other instruments which are not mentioned here; and the master surgeon will discover by himself his instrument, according to what his works and his experience show, for there are various diseases for which the old methods do not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if it breaks not from bone or other bones, or if it is crooked, if it seeks other instruments, as I have said, and helps with gestures, as is its form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone, that it does not slip, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is slight, if the grasp has all of these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not match its natural form, and the shape is unsightly, and even in women of gentle birth, if one should think that it is hidden within the tooth, and is not in its rightful place, and one cannot soothe it or support it: then it must be extracted; and if it is foreign to the tooth, if one grasps this instrument which has this shape, which is like a small beak, and is made of iron without a groove at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And it must be grasped firmly and cautiously with the hands just as long as the tooth lasts, and because of that one must not move the others, and if it appears, it can be limed, if one uses a file like this which has the same shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is just like making nails; and while holding the tooth firmly and cautiously with the hands, if it moves even slightly, if it cries out, the tip should be filed off at the end when it is finished, for if it is too deep it bites the tongue, if one should file away the roughness as much as it is equal, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth before the jaw is loose, by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot press against that which annoys him that it does not bleed, and you must treat him with restrictive medicines, which is of no use; if you must restrain it with a gold wire, because the silver wire turns green and swells, but the gum does not move; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, if you take hold of the wire and double it between the two front teeth, then place the teeth between the other teeth, if there are one or more of them, until you see clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; then finish the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand steadily and cautiously, until it does not move; and let the bandage be fixed to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the ends of the thread and gather them together, and put them between the sound teeth, and keep them close until they bleed no more; and then leave them close as much as they can stay in place, and if they slip or the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread; if it should remain and serve close at hand, and this is the form of a knot and the figure of the dressing of the two thumbs, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth bites, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and do not let anything interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make its form like that of a chipped tooth, and put it back in its place or the default is there, and strain it as we have said, and remain and serve steadily for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is this thread that comes from the outside of the tongue or nature that is not born close at hand; or by chance of a deep wound; and the work is such that you must cover the mouth of the patient, and place your thumb in his mouth, and hold the tongue; then take hold of the large nerve as much as the tongue is displaced from its place, and if there is any delay or not, and this is the sign of a wound, if it has burst the vessel and taken hold of the large thread; and keep that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that is outside; and when you have done this, if you lift the limb of pink and easy, or of cold water, and put the tongue outside a little attempt of linen; and bind the patient tightly so that the limb cannot move.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood flows from the wound, take out the glass vial and break it; if it does not stop, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see pus of a color or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining to swell, and there is moisture, if it evacuates the clot, and you make a small incision, and deliver from one side and the other; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a clot and broil it until it is dry, then come back to your work until you have finished all your work; then lift the pale and thick blood, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes comes from the throat bones which are called "godath", and the seeds are two almonds; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is abscesses of small size and of soft color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron; but leave it until it is dead, and then you will remove it, or it will break by itself; and if it is pale in color and the root is thin, if you have brought the instrument to cover, but look first if the abscess has settled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	When thus he sits the patient before the sun, and his shoulder joint is in its proper place, he should cover his mouth with his hands and grasp the testicles between them, and press the tongue downwards to the utmost of his ability; and let there be silver or barley as subtle as a needle.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	...press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, as it is done; and let it be of silver or gold, just like a nail.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form: grasp the one of the nails with one tong, and the other with the other hand; and when you have grasped one nail, grasp the other in the same way, and then make an incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when the blood has drained, if there are still clots of blood, either break them up with pomegranate seeds, or burn them with bay leaves, or similar things, until the wound is clean; then cure as it is healed; and never again shall there be any other incision in the throat except for the two nails, if you grasp them just as the two nails remain intact.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was inside the throat, that is to say a small abscess; and she had it very close to the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and died if she lingered in that state for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two stones through the two holes that were inside.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had drunk too much, and had lain in one place a long time, then I felt a fire burning, and in that fire a great portion of my bow was consumed; then I put the rest on the other side where I did not feel the pain, and I closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I put the incision back into these abscesses, and I closed a part of it, and did not come out of it but a little blood; and in that place the lady who was accompanying me fainted, and when I began to drink water and wine, I could not stop vomiting from that place for a long time; and the abscesses were getting larger and filling up my belly as much as I could bear; so I bound them and cauterized them within the throat: after that I felt some sense of crossing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to me after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb descends at the shoulder, and it flees and is long, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is broad and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is sutured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the wound is appeased, and it is subtle, if you must, you must close it; and that which is round and complete and is not long; and that is bloody or of yellow or black colour, if you must avoid the incision of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, as I have said, by its stench and its length, you must make the patient sit in the sunlight, and press the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned before; then remove the burr from the limb, and close with two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two thumbs.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And must not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, you grieve the voice and the word. And after the incision, use what we have said concerning the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then must you use something to support the cauterization in the painful area
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery if it is acute is severe.

li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The signs of an abscess are, as one remembers from one place to another in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two methods by which it is manifested, one of which is similar to itself, and the other which is due to moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if the limb is hanging loose or it is fixed in place.

Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when a fracture comes from a joint, and it is left until it is fixed, by chance if it is corrupted the bone and the nerve of the joint, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.

Or if an incision is made at the principal part of the limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is middle-sized, it will go to the principal part of the limb; or if it is made at the foundation, if you pierce it when it is not middle-sized, it will cause fistula; and it cannot be cured in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are many diseases that contain moisture, and if there are maligns that do not obey the laws of health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case where you see a bone structure at the touch, and which is similar in color to flesh, and is soft from one side and not red as the marrow in the head or in the artery or the vein, and is not deep; if you must break it, you must break off a piece of the bone, and burn the soft part, and if you have to hold the two levers of the arm as we mentioned in the apostemes of the head; and the thumb and the little finger, and so you must take care not to damage the nerve or the vein, and not to cause swelling or bruising, only to grasp the hand, and do not speak too soon, that you do not break anything that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you puncture the vein or the artery, and this does not allow you to work, if you put into the wound a piece of vitriol glass shard, or some powder that remains bloodless, hold the wound; and leave it until the bleeding has ceased, and soften the wound, and begin to work again.

And when it is stained, if you return to your work until you have finished; then if you must indicate that there remain no small scabs, if you grasp and crush them.</start_of_turn>

And if there is in the root of the swelling a large vein, if you cannot do anything but grasp that swelling at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging loose; then apply pressure to the wound with a bundle of cotton soaked in Egyptian balsam, and then cure.</start_of_turn

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if you understand to cover the root of the thing, and to pull forward, and to bind as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez. de squinance	When the wound is well drained, if the dressing of oil covers the scar, while it is sound.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of the size of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	As for those who have a squinance, it is necessary that the flap of the throat which is called the epiglottis be freed; and this will not help, for all the veins and the blood vessels of the patient are at those who have placed their trust in it in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.</start_of_turn>
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the blood vessels, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from the strangulation.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary therefore, when our voices tear the epiglottis, that we cut it from the outside of three circles or four, a small cut through two circles or in the quantity of the cut through the cartilage; and if it reaches the epiglottis, if it is consistent with the section of the epiglottis, there will be no swelling, and the veins will be long.</start_of_turn

If the master is fearful, if you can, extend the skin of the throat over the entire circumference; then open the vein as far as it goes to the nail; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see nothing; and then close the vein as before; and demonstrate by the section of the nail that the spurting blood comes from the broken vessel, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is still doubt about the strangulation, assemble the four limbs of the wound together, and bind them all firmly with the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing, until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The abscess does not cease until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged dead, and the flaw is left behind.</start_of_turn
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglottis in order that the patient does not vomit; and let him breathe through the wound; and this is kept as a safeguard against death; and in order to command the old man to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then it is commanded to suture the wound and cure it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a woman who had swallowed a needle, and she choked on it, and a piece of her throat was torn away; and I went to call for help, and I found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it, and saw that it did not reach any vein or artery except for the throat, and that it was coming from the wound itself.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and saw to the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and the woman did not suffer further except that she lost her voice, and returned home well; for in the making of the epiglottis there was no fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "throat hernia," and are great abscesses the color of butter, and are very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; or naturally there is no cause
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is in two ways: one is like fat, as we have seen; and the other way is like an abscess which comes from an artery; and there is danger, and one must not attempt to do anything fierce except in a small area, and must probe and explore thoroughly: if you find it like pure fat and not in any vein, if you touch it, if like us, and take away the surrounding tissue if there is none; and encircle well around, and cure as it should be until it is completely healed
des nous	And encircle all around, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many are the ways we are deceived, of which I will speak; and know that I will tell you the difference between a false and a true statement.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the cause of dislocation is heat and fever that lasts as long as the inflammation persists, and is accompanied by swelling; therefore let the fever and heat rest.

With regard to the newly born, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains its own sac, which is like the colour of mustard, and it begins like a pea, and becomes large; and they are like wax or fat or moisture, and the colour is such as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the knot, to ask and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissaires," according to their form or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire about abscesses of the body is that you take more moisture than you find in the abscess, and press your thumbs and index fingers until you believe that the instruments have felt the knot; then that it be according to the greatness of the abscess; then withdraw the introducer, and take care that the surrounding area does not bleed
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes too close to the surface, that is to say when it appears, if the surrounding area does not receive moisture, the blood that is thick, if it appears in a cross, take hold of it with your thumb and forefinger, and press it lightly from the inside outwards, and hold the area where you are working with the other hand; and if you do not hold it firmly, take it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If nothing remains, if it comes back many times; if it bleeds again, if it does not grieve you, if you employ corrosive powders at the wound, hold the wound steady and put on soothing things above; and if it is great, if you cut out two fingers of the wound, and cure what is causing the pain.

Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the entromittent instruments, and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three kinds: great, medium, and small, to embrace the fistulas; and they are like needles which we sew with wounds, and they are of saffron, or iron, or silver, and must be of gold which is yellow, and are more proven of black pitch to embrace the cortices of fistulas; and they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the needles are of the same shape as seeds, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if the needles have two cortices of three kinds each; and if the needles have three cortices, and are of three kinds; and if the needles have two cortices, and a single cortice only, and are of three kinds; all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of the humerus is fractured, and some of them are cut only from one side, from which we protect the nerves, because of this we do not ligate the vein or the nerve; and these are the substances which are restored in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them when the incisions are made; and they are of three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and we do not use them for any other purpose than for bones such as the leg, arm, elbow, and shoulder, and similar things; and no other instrument is ever made so small, resembling the bristles of a brush, as in this form, because in this way we stop the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one must never put it back in the same place where it has already grasped the veins, and arteries, never again in such a great form.

des apostemes des asselles	As for the incisions of the armpits, abscesses, wounds, and extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, there are often evacuations of blood in these operations; and where there is doubt and fear, many die.

When the head of the shoulder is dislocated from moisture, and is reset but does not stay in place, it dislocates repeatedly with the slightest movement, as we have seen; therefore one must first reset the dislocation.

de la routure de l’artere	of the route of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.
