des apostemes des ners	Des apostemes des ners.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	The fire cautery instructs the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And thus it often happens with adjuvants and those who are two or more in their limbs or joints, that there are after-wounds, and their colour appears like that of old gold, and is in many situations accompanied by pain; and when it is strained, if the patient feels pain, it is not because of gold, but because of blood; and it swells well from all sides, neither going forward nor backward, neither up nor down, and that which is in the joints does not cover with iron: by chance there will be contraction; and if that which is on the shoulder or the elbow or the forehead is grasped too tightly, it makes the skin taut.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the after-wound is small, if the vein has one staple, and it is held at its root; and if it is large, if the clot is at the bone, and it is pulled out, then the bone is fractured and the wound is sutured at the suture, and the cure is made as long as it is healthy
des grosses boces pendans	From the armpits downwards.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never has it happened in the belly and never elsewhere that there has been such a disease as this one which is called "funge" because of its likeness to a worm, and its root is subtle, and its head is great; and in it there are both small and great spots. I have seen two men who had two or three of these in their bellies which appeared more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had white roots, and their heads were split open, and corrected with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I saw two of these in the belly, one of XVIII ounces and the other of VI and three-quarters, and in the incision if you look to see if the patient is moist, the color of the blood is pale and moist with white roots; if the wound reaches the large spleen, and you are present, apply the fire cautery.</start_of_turn>
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the hip comes often too great a discharge of blood, and if it does not go away, if you hasten, then indeed burn; and if you see the patient groaning and faint from the incision of the flesh, take a thread of silk well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then the restraint, and do not cease draining the thread of silk until it has closed the artery, and do the work by it; and if the roots are tough, if there is fear in the belly, but you must indeed cover half, then burn that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep that you only cover the hair which is of loose colour and of bad sense and of milk-yellow pus.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For indeed it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is fierce.</start_of_turn
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling appears from burn of wound or fracture of bone, and is on the belly and there are some bones there, as it happens in other ways, or blood which clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or windiness; and if it is by the route of the bone and by the issue of the bowel, if it is the colour of the abscess, it is a light thing with pain, and opens from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If by the escape of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when one presses it there, if it returns and then recurs, and by chance if it is closed, and brings about great swelling at the entrance of the bath and much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to moisture, it is a light matter; press firmly with your hand and do not constrain me. If it is due to blood, if there are large and hard clots, they are fixed in quantity. If it is due to wind, if the pulse is strong, and the work is done when the source of the pain is identified as either a vein or an artery or the wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you leave the cure as it is.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or as the chapter on blood clots mentions, concerning the artery and the vein.</start_of_turn>
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If the intestine or the belly is the source, command the patient to hold his breath, and keep his hand stretched out, then mark with a finger the most prominent part of the swelling; then grasp the swelling between your hands, and bring the thumb to cover half of the swelling; then join the thumb to the index finger and hold it firmly; then take half of the swelling and place your thumb on the line and mark the place where the index finger touches, and where the intestine is; if you find the intestine caught in the line, if you pull, release the intestine from the belly; if you find the belly, if you grasp the swelling, and cut off the excess; if the artery or the vein is injured, if it flows too much, go back to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have done in the form of a cross that you think will cause the pain to cease; then strain the swelling for three periods over the needles, and if you see the bone, break the needles, and leave the limb as long as it swells, and cut off the dead part by itself; or you can remove it when it has become discreet and soft, and cure the limb of what is necessary, and bandage the swelling as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and stitch the limb.</start_of_turn>
dou chancre	sore abscess
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have already spoken of the signs of an abscess, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how to shun the cautery. We say that an abscess swells in the marrow, and has great caution in its treatment. The old men say that when an abscess is in the flesh or can be scraped out like an abscess which is in marrow, and in the heel, and in other parts, it must be extirpated as soon as possible; and when it is large and old, if it cannot be brought about, do not approach it, for I know of no cure for it. None of them has ever cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And in the work, when it is in the flesh or can be extirpated, as we have said, do not purge the black bile from the patient once. Then make the patient well again if there is any visible swelling. Then give the patient a purgative, such as wine, to make the work easier. Then take out the nails or abscesses, and the sinews of all parts, and the bone of all parts round about; and leave the wound to heal naturally. Expect the wound to bleed at the incision of the artery or vein if the cautery is done too much; then cure with another remedy until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said above in the division of these signs of hydrophobia, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of congestion resemble, and the cure which is made by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: if only the lightning is alight; and one must not touch iron in these two signs: that is to say, tympanites and icterus, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you are treating this sign of hydrophobia which is called "lightning" of medicine, and the cure does not profit, if you observe that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides hydrophobia, as with all solution of the belly and similar things; if you do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient with great fortitude, and he has only hydrophobia, and he is not too young nor too old, if you must work: take hold of the patient's right hand in your hands, and the minister presses the belly at the end of the water towards the lowest part down to the heel, then take the thumb and index finger according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenchant of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And be trenchant of two parts, at a point, and in all other respects be not so much entrained that it can come down to the intestines when it is grasped, and cannot be staunched; then look if hydrosis is ingrained towards the intestines: if it is suspected that it is caused by bile, make an incision on the left side of the third ventricle; and if it is caused by the disease of the liver, make an incision on the right side; and if it is caused by moisture, make an incision on the left, and do not be afraid that the patient lies on the incision that the supernumeraries do not run to that feeble limb; then pierce the skin with the instrument, and grasp the gut, and keep your hand over the palm of your hand between the skin and the pericardium as though you were grasping the quantity of an nail or the like; then pierce the pericardium until the palm of your hand comes to the seventh part, and that is the measure of the water, then draw out the water, and there is left this instrument which is like this form.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver nail, and is of flaxseed or elderberry seed, and at the lower part there is a small hole; and where it costs one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head of the nail is cut off as with a knife, and this is the shape of the incision that the writer makes to cut off the head.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	And at the top of all this is the bolster, so that when the instruments come to the acute, if you drain them now above the instrument; empty half or a third part, for if you drain more than that which can be contained in that hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will vomit, or he will approach death; but drain according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then take out the instrument and retain the acute, and it is retained now by the spur which stamps the hole which is above the facet, as I have said, that you pierce according to this manner; then return the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering this, and take out a small quantity of the acute; do this neither way, and keep using it until it no longer stays.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient, and you see him drink water, if the physician applies a poultice or sand cautery, and by drinking sweat or bath and sun, and if you keep him from drinking; and the physician gives him drying medicines until he is cured, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Do nothing foolish, and keep following until there remains only a little water left. And if you doubt the patient, and you let him drink too much water, if the recruit of the sepulture or the warm sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and take care to drink; and the recruit of drying medicines until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without having a hole in the belly, or the hole is small, or it is not completely in its place.

puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or pierce the hole quite deeply with a large needle, and tie and keep it closed for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if you leave it closed, he will urinate, and then you can remove it; and by chance, it will not be necessary, for the urine that comes out will not leave the hole closed
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, if it is treated with lead weights, as we have said, if it dilates.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who have no hair at the root of the hair are bald, for none are born with hair at the root of the beard, since they cannot urinate until they lift their beard up; and they cannot urinate because of that which matters does not reach the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of this work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, and the head of the thigh and the hip are as wide as a thumb, if the opening is in the middle, as it should be; and you must take care of the evacuation of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des pustules de la verge	of the thigh
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this white spot appears on the verge, and is a sign of a harmful disease; and in it there are both malignant and benign things. Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the bath is malignant, with a dark color and discharge, it is necessary to apply cautery to it
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat the whole limb, if it is not firmly secured, the head of the shoulder will be pierced; and comes black bile and corruption to its root and marrow; if you do not remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranate trees and sometimes, then treat with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood clots come, if you mix the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is of two kinds: for blood clots, and for corruption. If the head of the shoulder is corrupted and drawn back, if you bite or draw out the hair a span of plum, and the patient urinates; and when the hair has fallen out around the head of the shoulder which has not been circumcised, or if there is wound or incision, if you do not then immediately singe the instrument that chews, until the limb is freed, and deliver the hair from all parts; and if this be impossible, if you do not immediately singe at the spur of the moment, put on a strip of linen soaked in cold water, that it should not be disturbed.
de la circoncision	If it is an urgent matter to separate this, if you can, grasp it immediately without causing any harm to the head of the thigh or the heel; then slowly separate between the thumbs, and put a wet linen bandage on it with cold water, so that it does not slip out of place.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely an act of continuing care like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and properly as possible, if it is necessary that we make it as mild as possible for the patient.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach me circumcision of the children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have learned only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen that the greatest part of masters and doctors who practiced circumcision did so without knowledge, with force, and with a new instrument; if it happened that the testicles escaped because of two layers of skin, and by chance if one cut through these and left the other behind
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it returns covered, and the pain is doubled, and there is the mutilation which is more than doubtful concerning the tip of the limb; and the mutilation of the bone by chance escapes the wound, and repairs the work, and many times happens that they must undergo mutilation without having had to do so, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the modification which is made with force throughout the thread I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces tear just as well downwards as upwards.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equal in all directions, but the thread is well stretched around the skin; and if the movement is gentle from the outset, as if you were thinking of a child, if he understands, do not force him to bind the thread around the limb only slightly, but do so thoroughly in all ways; then draw it straight between your hands or remove your fingers so that the boy does not see them, neither any instruments; then hold your hand at the root and breathe or cough, and pull up as much of the thread as is necessary; then tie it firmly with two knots at the pouch and the must index, and clip between the two threads, then keep the thumb relaxed and pull out the chief of the limb; then let the blood flow back naturally as much as it can, for that is the treatment; and sprinkle powder on and over the powder a bandage glued with egg white from rose hips, confirmed with rose oil and balsam, and leave it on until the other side is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	When the limb is deformed in this way: the two bones are tense and bent, and the limb is as thick as a sleeve,
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of deformation is when the marrow is fractured during the incision; therefore it is necessary to stretch your nail so that the wound is open; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold your nail firmly, even if you grasp it tightly, and then cut.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they trespass for two days, and that which is from the root is swollen, if you leave it as long as the spasms subside, and the swelling is slight; if you press it as you can, and hold on to the root, it will avail you nothing.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you press too much over and above measure, and it goes away, it will avail you nothing; cure it as we have said, while it is still sound.</start_of_turn>
dou retenement de l’urine	because of the retention of urine.</start_of_turn>
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine if it is from the obstruction of a stone, or of blood congealed, or of a bowel, or of chaff, or of similar things, which we have mentioned in the preceding; and if the urine is not dripped away, and you see that the retention is caused by the stone which is in the loin or the neck of the bladder, if it is possible that the patient is bent over his knees; and let him put his feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part under his back, and restrain the patient so that he cannot move as much as he can; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is dripped away; and if it does not come, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, if it is possible that you administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “syringes”, of which this is the form: either of silver with a legiger chick pea, like the head of a bird; or of the caine of a long and half palm, or of silver at the chief.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus it is done with a double thread, and at the head of it a thumb of wool or cotton, and bind the thumb to the thread in the syringe; and cut away the excess of the wool and bind up to the head of the syringe; then join the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the chair; and raise the bladder and the belly with oil moist and oily with olive oil and urine; then put the syringe lightly into the belly, as far as it reaches the root of the belly; then double the belly downwards towards the buttocks; then pull back the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel that it has gone until it is empty; and this is not done except in this order because of what it brings or what it goes out with is twisted; then cut the thread at the top and at the bottom, and the urine follows the thread, and it is pulled out forcefully, and correct the urine; and start the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are urine stones or blood in the bladder, or if it is filled with pus, and you see urine and medicines boiling, if you do everything that is called a «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three punctures: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped so that the medicine can be pressed down firmly along the limb, if we can manage to expel the moisture, and push outwards when necessary; and when you see the medicines oozing from the bladder, put the head of the stretcher in the moisture, and push outwards from there; if you push the moisture outwards, and then push inwards strongly from there; if the moisture enters there, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle cluster from which the bladder is clustered.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from one side or the other it is split; then take a bladder of mutton and put the moisture into it which you see clustering the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a double bow, and burn one half of that moisture over the fire; then withdraw the head of the cluster from the limb, then strain your hand over the bladder until all the moisture has drained out, as long as the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it round the edge; then draw the string firmly through these punctures, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a doll, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and tie it up with the instrument; and do as you would with a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned above the methods of handling stones, and their extraction with medicines; and we have spoken of the difference between a stone that is embedded as rain and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened according to its size; and in the bladder, and the kidney; and I shall tell you openly and briefly about them.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder is oftener loose, and this is a sign that it has burst from the bladder as much as from its subtlety; and it opens gravel, and grinds the patient’s flank, and causes them to urinate frequently, and then becomes hardened; and from these bursts there is always some sediment; and the foundation is easily loosened for about three years, and is more grievous in the old, and is as common in youths as in old people; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first cleanse the patient with vinegar, to remove all the poison that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never fails to ask for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the limbs, loosen and move down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and it does not rise again; then make him sit between your hands and his hands are at his thighs, so that the bladder is fully emptied downwards; then ask and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten to cut above the stone immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not move on touching with the whole hand, if more oil from the left hand, if the patient is fat, or if more from the middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; then push it down to its foundation and ask for the stone, and when you feel it with your middle finger, if the bladder is tight at the neck; then press above your middle finger, and push down the stone until it comes out or you see it cut through
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the hairs above, and with his left hand grasp the skin that is below the hairs in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge with a clap, for thus is its form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And between what is between the ribs and the navel, do not go into the middle but at the cost of the left side; and be two above the navel, and your two below either together or on the navel, and be the size that will traverse if it be wide by fault, and within narrow, according to the quantity of the navel, do not go too great; by chance the pressure if it must be on the navel or on the foundation, that it leap forward in its work; and the nails that are in the part of the navel or that are angled, and margins: if it is grasped to sit; and if there is part that is soured, it is like a gland, round, from which issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there is an angle and margins, make the size greater; and if it does not leap, it is certain that you must strain on the tendons which are like a file at the head, for the muscle must strain the navel if it does not escape; or you can use a blunt instrument curved at the head; and if you do not succeed in engaging it, if it is too wide, or if the flesh hangs loose, if it is a straining of vitriol; and if there are several nails, strain out the greatest at the belly of the bladder first, then stretch upwards, then stretch outwards, and the smaller afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is large, if you cover it with wool, and make it more painful.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	If it is large, if you cover it with wool, and make it more painful. For in this case two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes to him again because his testicles cannot withstand it; but whatever you do, if you tear it out by pieces, while you are tearing it out, as long as you finish your work, if you apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and hold it, and put upon it a wet bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the burning; then raise the patient up on his collar and do not loosen the thread until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have pulled it [the dislocated shoulder], if there is much pain in the limb from oil and water, then cure it with dynafinicon oil and balsamic oil until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	If pus comes out of the wound and corruptions, and blood clots in the bladder, and either because of that the urine is retained, which is known in part as without jumping with the urine: if so then drain your urine from the wound, and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away; then raise the wound with water and ease and silk, and help him in every way you can, as long as he is sane; and know that all the times you cure him, that you must tie the two stitches and gather the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small, and it is in the bladder or the tube of the kidney, and is fixed, and the urine cannot issue; if the doctor knows what I say, that you must urinate many times, we shall hear of the size for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved this to be true.</start_of_turn>
