de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the limb with one hand and with the other grasp the bone above and below, then place your thumb between the two joints, and pull forcefully, loosening the ligament, and move the blood clot which is in the wound; and cure as long as it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is dislocated in women, and this happens only once, it is a serious ailment which is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that no woman knows who has seen her uncover herself as much as she does, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	If by chance one cannot find a woman who knows this art of hands, then the fourth method is that if the woman’s thumb is thicker than the man’s, because it can make a deeper cut, and there is great fear of that. If necessary be aware of this, if you take a woman who knows, and mark the thumb on her, and if you do not mark it, know that I cast aside the subtle art; and present her with a woman who knows a part of this art, and command that she do what you command of her by the inquiry of the thumb; and look well whether the woman is a virgin. For if she is, she will push out her thumb or foundation and question the thumb; and if she finds it, restrain her thumb with her left hand.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If it is true, as soon as it moves from the belly to the knee, as far as it reaches the hip bone; then close the incision at the hip bone where it appears, and feel the bone in that part; do not move the thigh above the bone or below, and keep the incision small at first. Then gradually widen the incision, until you feel the bone is no longer painful. Many kinds of stones are like this: small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those that have rains.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if the stones resemble each other, it is known that they are pus.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go away, if you put at the limb vitriol broken, and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the bone is healed, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone at your home to help you in your work; and if it does not go away, and it is the artery that is cut, if you put powder on the limb and strain with thread and bandage, and do not start again, and leave the bone alone, except by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of blood is calmed and the limb is relaxed, if you return to this work while the wound is still open.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white wax, which is as soft as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "wax," and never is it properly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that it is not otherwise. And it is the skin of the seed between the white wax that we have said. That does not happen by chance.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ramus is weak and comes from the seeds, and that matter is spread out
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if percussion comes from the joints, and this moisture if it has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are the signs of corruption in this assembly, for if it is white as snow or as we have said, if the abscess is round like an egg, and it does not split open, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very flesh, if the abscess is round with a part of the yolk, and because of this some people think that it is one egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white substance, if one feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it is like all the intestines that are put together, as we have said.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, which follows the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When our burnings are done by iron, if it be known that the patient be well according to the measure of his power and the filling of his body; then we apply it upon his back, upon something somewhat high, and put pieces of cloth under his shoulders; then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend the limb to one of the two costles below the ribs; then we take the sponge dipped in oil, and burn the skin of the ribs among those which are long until we reach the navel; and let the burn be made straight by dividing the skin of the ribs up to the white spot, and burn it thoroughly according to the measure of his power; then we pierce the belly with a needle at a large opening, and drain all the fluid, and then we put on our sponges, and draw up the belly; and do not touch the ribs, but only the belly; burn all or in pieces immediately the cost of it, if you do not burn it thoroughly, the fluid will return; and if the urine spurts forward from your work, let it remain in its place when you have completed the work of the belly. Then assemble the two leaves of the ribs at a costure, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the urine corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the veins that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut off the limb at the whole suspension, drain the urine, and cure it like we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if it is acute and gathered into two parts together, the threads which are two branches; if you join the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood away and put in the wound a layer of fine linen soaked in oil of roses; and put another layer of fine linen soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the two bones, and put under doubled cloths, and bind it up according to this fashion:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and use coarse wool yarn according to this likeness and be assembled with needlework at the neck of the braies; and one of the bones grasps on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the tender part; and the other two teeth on the two angles, and be all assembled the restriction in the loop of the brazier; and in no way is medicine this thread of cautery in place of the size of iron, and only take one surgical cautery needle, and join the skin of the bones, and if done as we have said, if the white substance which contains the blood is discovered; if you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that membrane as we have mentioned, and burn it with this subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And so do all the physicians in every way that you can, until you have scraped away all of it; and keep the fire away from the yolk; and scrape that this work is more salve; and guard diligently from falling out of place of blood, and more than the works of size; and if anything else hinders you, or incisions or falling out of place of blood or anything else, if it hinders you, do that which hinders you, according to what is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you anticipate perforation, as I have said, and you are certain by the meanings that we have said that the moist blood is limpid, if you make the patient sit on a low seat; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with a wide span, and make the perforation long from the bone; and if the hole is large, let the blood flow out completely; then put a cotton pad over the wound, and bind it, and leave to drain the remaining blood, and cure until the wound is healed; and if the white blood does not drain from the wound, as you must drink a spoonful or the instrument used for treating the hydropic swelling, as it is formed above; and enlarge the wound, and scrape that the blood comes back, and assemble after six months or when the pain has ceased, and when it is assembled as before, and then the patient will be able to resume his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the incision of the hip bones
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The hairs that are in this root area are few in number; it seems to me that they are worth leaving alone; and I will tell you about the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that main and forearm come or swell, and sometimes there are coions; and this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive heat and moisture, which is spread as coions or percussion; and is the color of an abscess according to the color of the flesh; and does not cause pain, and is an abscess of grief; and by chance is a bloody abscess full of pus and blood, with a foul color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the disposition of the heat of the abscess, when you press it with your hand; and I do not advise you to touch it
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made to swell a vein is known by his attitude at the expression of pain in the thighs; and may well do the same size as this semblance, and on the other thighs; and it is that you grasp tightly like nails, then the egg is high, and the thread is of white silk, and release the suspension from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already swollen with these thighs, if you must then treat the egg and grasp it; and if it is towards the silk or in the vessels, if you must deliver all that is tense, and grasp roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the cartilage comes loose from the bone or remains behind, if you must grasp it all, and pull out the root, as we have said
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is finished, if you apply a dressing of coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then bandage the wound until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the incision of the hip bones
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering similar to an eyelid, with the softening of the nails, and the patient groans loudly when it moves; and the cure for this ailment is well known as well as this one mentioned before, and all that we have said concerning it is sufficient
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on the edge of the bed, then hold the suspenders of the clothes around his waist at his thighs, to all the vessels that are close to the hip, and grasp the master, and extend them forth; then cut with a sharp knife wide enough to pierce through the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then drain from the buttocks, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert a needle or double thread, and tie it to the first root or where the vein has come from, and tie it firmly at the other root; then cut around the middle directly, following the length of the bone, and remove the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as usual or apply a bandage, so that no vessel has been damaged that does not need to bleed; for if all the vessels come loose, if you pull out the stitches, it will be enough to draw out the wound from all the vessels; so that it does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and that it dries and does not suffer further.
de la routure dou syfac	If the oes does not lose its nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell, they will not aid.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The event of this branch is by section that comes or by swelling above the belly in the part of the intestines; for the intestine descends from that passage to one of the buttocks; and that passage is either by swelling or by extension of the limb, and these two methods cause it: by percussion, or by jumping, or by pressure, or by the elevation of grief faith, and by similar things; and the sign when it is by swelling of the swelling, is that there is swelling both above and below, in long tension, and does not come immediately; and the abscess is equal until towards the navel, for that is what the swelling of the swelling presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the scapula is sectioned, that it immediately causes pain at the shoulder, and the scapulae are different in position, from the edge to the skin, because of the displacement of the intestines and the hardness of the scapula.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does the bone move with the intestine, and is retained when it is held, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cures with fear, for fear of them, it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient urges that the intestine be returned to its place in the wound if it can enter; then either hold your thumb on its collar between your hands, and keep the buttocks; then extend the knee upwards, and grasp all the skin of the buttocks long; then open the wound from the navel to the thighs; and leave out the intestines as large as the thumb according to what you must do to open the wound, and as much as it can be; then press the swelling that is under the skin of the buttocks until the thick swelling is discovered from all parts; then place your index finger where the buttocks are joined, between the white swelling which is under the skin of the heel and between the second swelling, and withdraw that which is behind the heel, and between the second swelling; and then move your thumb inwards of the buttocks, and place the white swelling at the top of your left hand, and keep the heel against all the swelling; and command the minister to extend the heel upwards, and loosen that which is behind the band; and ask at your sides if there is any intestine or thick swelling that has not been discovered, and if you find nothing, if the wound is in front; then take a needle or make a large stitch of X threads, and pass it in the back part of the swelling which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the size, then grasp the threads that appear from the needle, until there are three threads; then assemble them in the form of a cross and tie the swelling, of which we have said is under the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of two parts; then cover the threads with the skin, and tie them in two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except for the wound itself; and put back the thread according to the first thread along two fingers; and after these two threads leave the swelling that is under the buttocks the greatest of a finger; and after all the rest according to the roundness of the heel; then grasp in the part which is under the skin of the buttocks, as much as without injury, and bow it, as we have said before; then apply coarse wool soaked in oil, and put in the wound, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never burn the fat surrounding the wound as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, it often happens that blood flows out due to an open vein; and if it is delayed at the root, whether from a sudden swelling or from a hot liquid, put on what we have said above until it flows; then close the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this limb I never saw anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And some old folks say that it is made like a twig which is bound to the nut, in part like tying up blood vessels, after the size above lightly downwards; then close the wound, and cure the abscess of that which caused it, until the blood vessels flow; and close the wound as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes out whole from anger, as we have said, and open the eyes; and do not touch any intestines as they are connected, and if you touch them, that is enough, and repair them at all times; and if it remains too long in this place, if you believe the wound or the spleen, because the intestines are departing; and this comes from the extension of the spleen which is in anger, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and relaxed the eyes and open; and close the wound as we have said before; and never closed with iron in this manner: let the patient lie still on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the fracture inflated with a large measure of three fingers; then withdraw the spleen which is from the leather that covers it, then take the needle and push it out the limb that appears from the spleen; and press at the bottom of the belly, then close the two wounds that appear from the spleen on the top of the needle; and close one and the other. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you are done with the stitching, if the wound is closed and cured, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The scab is constrained, and has no appearance in the course of treatment, and the burn is mute in this limb, and more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in households, because the bones that are inside are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie down on his back, and to scrape off the softened skin from the natural skin; then assemble the layers of skin with a bandage, and if you see it, close the first excess of softened skin with two or three stitches firmly; then scrape between the stitches, and cure as the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	The wounds which are customary in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to do so except in two cases: the first is that the guardian of the wound responds when asked, and gives an account of the cure; and the second, because we often mix up the branding of some beasts with our assistants, as with oxen and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that branding is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that way in which we do it by traction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the hair becomes soft and limp; then we grab it by the hand, until it is set and you no longer feel it
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the armpit: command that you hold the arm firmly, and press the skin of the armpits towards your left hand, then bind the sling, and grasp each exercise at its root, when you have well secured them; and leave no trace of blood or any clot that is on the vessels; and this method of cautery is more effective than that which is done by traction, for in traction remains by chance no hair, because it desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermofrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like this: one if between the two testicles there appears as much as the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in court he urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other kind if in women, and has on the navel as much as a penis and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And as for the cure for baldness and famine, if you see that the hairs are falling out completely, cure them like other wounds; in the second method, of those whose urine spurts through the pores of the skin, if there is no other cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphrodism is in accordance with two methods: one if between the two testes opens just like the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in their urine. And the other method if it is in women, and has on the navel just like a boy and two testes. And the cure of the tumor and envy if it is that you remove all the testicles, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second method, of men whose urine spurts through the skin of the testes, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The hair of the head is too dense on the natural part, so that it hinders vision; and many women have it as much as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to keep the superabundance of hair at hand or on the armpits, and to grasp it lightly; do not prick too deeply, for blood will flow, and it is better to leave the wound open than to close it when it is still bleeding; and another hair that comes out at the root of the beard, and the sweat, and by chance spurts out, and this is called the ancient "baldness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you suspect that it is displaced, if as we have said the tension is there, and the cure must be continued until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If the cause of the displacement is not clearly perceived, or if the wound is small; and if it is due to birth or an accident, or by a fracture caused by a foreign body, such as a nail, or by a bite of a dog, or by infection, or by any other cause; and if the wound is fresh, or if the fetus is still in the womb, or if there is suspicion of fracture, or if there is suspicion of disease, or if the child is feverish; then you must have a thorough examination of the wound and the surrounding area.</start_of_turn>
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the patient is conscious and the wound is nearby, if there is swelling at the shoulder or elbow.</start_of_turn
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If he has a swollen swelling and it is close to two fingers, do not be hasty; take hold of your two thumbs and place one hand on his back, spreading out his legs; then stretch out the two fingers as long as the swelling is round and firm; then take hold of the swelling, and pour oil over it, and put it on the swelling, and keep the woman still at ease.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	If the swelling is hard and thick, it is to be suspected that there is a swelling resembling a piece of holly leaves.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If swelling has become soft, if you hang it up and press; and have medicines that abate blood, such as acacia, dragon’s blood, incense, together with many eggs; then administer a broad mustard plaster, so that the wound cannot stick together; and let it be long, and add a compress of dried lint; then let it heal naturally.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	When the armpit comes to bear, if it is covered according to this method, except for incisions made with hooks.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the armpit swelling which is in the armpit, one must not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are the opening of veins which, without custom, always accompany swelling; and when the hemorrhoids are old they become painful; and we have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms, and I will say those which follow the cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the armpit, when they are inflamed in the armpit, and they do not appear on feeling, except for the cure by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the armpit, which we can feel, are those which we can cure
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	If the woman is put in a cold house, and the alternum is tightly held at its roots, and the head is placed in its sockets, then sprinkle over medicines that restrain blood, such as chamomile and dragon’s blood and incense, and the like; then close her eyes for an hour, then put her in cold water; and when she recovers, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and the like, and then take oatmeal, and mix it with honey and beeswax, and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if she vomits, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this does not help, if she blows wind from her belly and has chills with fever; then take linen, wet it in juice of plantain or in vinegar with old wine, and blow air into her body.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, if the cure lies in draining it while it is sound; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a dark hair, if you cover it as I have said before; and then the cure while it is sound.
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are open veins which without support are usually not accustomed; and when old become tough. And we have said previously concerning the signs and symptoms, and I shall say those which remain to cure. I say that emoroids and tough skin, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except with the cure by iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the needle steady, grasp its root, then sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw the pieces an hour later, then put them into cold water; and if it bleeds, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and yeast, and make one application upon her back. And if it clots, that is good. If not, if it is bleeding profusely, put on a bandage at the back and has large wounds; then take lint, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of elderberry with wine old, and make it bleed. And when the incision is healed, if the wound is oily until it is healed; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the tough skin; and then it is healed until it is healed. And the after-effects of the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come about in the belly, as with boils and pimple abscesses and herpes and worms and swellings and fistulas and haemorrhoids and burned abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say that I mean the burned abscess which comes about in the belly, which is not like other abscesses which collect pus; and if you know the work of fire, look if the abscess is still in its infancy, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you see it
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	When thou seest the shoulder dislocated by moisture, and it is reset but will not hold, do not hasten to pierce; but make the patient sit upright while the pain subsides; then make the patient sit on two cushions or a chair, and support his back and join his limbs so that his knees are spread out, and put his arms down by his knees, and bind them firmly with a cord. Then push the shoulder backwards towards the costal margin, and insert the instrument from which we remove the cause of the pain at the root of the malady; and know that when you see the instrument being inserted, that you must first assess the depth of the wound so that what enters does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, know that you must cover the depth of the wound with a cloth so that the instrument does not cause pain; and know that you must put the cap of the instrument at the base and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the swelling bursts open, and we grasp the hand low, if it covers the head, at the elbow; and when the wound is emptied, if you wish to cleanse the wound, put in some soft cotton wool soaked in rose oil or in dry green oil; place the cotton firmly at the bottom of the wound, and put above the wound and above the wrist a layer of fine linen wool soaked in water or mallow, which must be cooked; then cauterize after two days following this, until it is healed; and never remove the dressing and the wound by flushing with water and honey, and then with water or leech and alum, which must be cooked.

de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mestier is first at play when she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down upon her belly, and desire to smell the armpit: then the child hastens to be born; then she delivers the head, and supports it with her hand; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on her belly, so that the child is thrust out; for when he descends upon his head, if he is supported by her hand, and the mare is quieted by her excess, this is not naturally born.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes from her feet, or comes from her horn or arm, or from her belly, or from behind, and is converted by chance from her collar, and by other wicked figures; if she is mistress of the play, that she is wise and discreet in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures that will help her.</start_of_turn>
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child is born naturally through the birth canal, and the woman gives birth, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a stool, or the women hold her; and as soon as she has relaxed her oil or vernix caseosa, then put her in the water between her two thighs where it is formed:

de l’issue des gemelz	it must be immediately corrected.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient. de plusors enfans	Moreover.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are they formed in the marshalling I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the glorious sage, and it must be that the sage dance all that, because by chance similar things happen; do as it is fitting
de l’enfant mort	From childhood death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman with a dead child or a miscarriage, if she does not go into labor, and you are compelled to work with your hands; if you suspect that the woman is of sound health, and has no accident or fear of death; if you suspect that the woman is lying on her back, and her shoulders are slumped forward, and her legs are lifted; then take hold of her wrist with two fingers, or bind her to the bed if she is not receiving treatment in the delivery of the child; then wipe her mouth with a cloth dampened with oil, mixed with alum and fennel seeds and flaxseed; then anoint her hands with these oils and these substances; then put them back into the womb lightly; then watch her closely or let her watch the attendants who are competent for this, and take care that the child does not appear to descend from her head; if she stretches out her fingers in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or on her face or her beard or her mustache or her teeth, and if she descends from her navel, if she grasps or writhes and has loose bowels; and take hold of the navel with your right hand, and put your elbow between her two left fingers, and hold her tightly with your whole left hand, and insert the navel into none of the places that we have mentioned, until it comes out naturally; and this is the form of the navel.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the heel finds itself another bone, or the third if you are dealing with it, so that the extraction is even; and then extend them evenly by moving from one side to the other, for the most part, or hold the nails with the teeth for the most part.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains stuck, if one sees a little of its fat coming out, and holds it in that place, and treats the other part; and if there is no fat remaining, if you put this bone or the higher one in its place, and do this until it comes out whole.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be retracted due to the stretching, then you must cover the drape with your thumb, until it comes out whole; then pull in the limb at the ankle or the knee, and then you must do the same with the other hand, and have two nails
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the shoulder is great and is strained at the issue, or if there is much pain in the joint, if you can, put the spinous process between your thumbs and hold the pain and strain it out; or you can rotate it with the instrument called "almidach," with which the bone comes out with the bones or the chapter that follows this one; and do the same for the fetus; then break the ribs as tenacious as they are, and the head of the shoulder will leap out by force, as long as the moisture is either coming out or has come out; and if it cannot be expelled, if it breaks into pieces at the breastbone, if you must; and if it is swollen in the belly or along the ribs, if you can, let the moisture escape as much as possible.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on its side, if the limb is attracted downwards, and the approach to the mouth of the wound is easier.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is strained in the belly or the arm, if you can, draw it out with the drape that surrounds the hand; and strain the belly or the arm, as long as the moisture that is there escapes; and if other members are stiff and the limb remains immobile, if you see its hand mark the marrow, and treat it until the marrow comes out whole; then put in oil or two, and force it out; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by a thick scab that has come, if you cannot pass it, you must bring moisture and fat things; and you must give it butter and moist things.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant's head is on his chest, and you put it even, if you remember what we said about the living child; and if you do not heed this, if his head should break apart piece by piece, do not leave anything of the second kind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if you remember what we said above about the matters that arise in the marshes; and if blood comes from the wound, if it be put in water that restricts, and you remember other cures.</start_of_turn>
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom a fetus had died, then consulted another concerning it, and refuted the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came an abscess in the belly, and it grew so large that it burst, and began to cause great pain.</start_of_turn>
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to seek help, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.</start_of_turn
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong dressing, and out came a bone, and after that some days another.</start_of_turn
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at you, for your belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wish the wound, and with hands of bone, as long as the woman was in a better state; and saw the woman long tense to the limit; and that was a little bow of blood in the leu; and I have never remembered this chapter except for this that when the master found a strange thing, that he should seek help.</start_of_turn
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, which we call books; and at this time there are two tears of blood from two veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Whatever the horn is more subtle than restrictive, or made of ebony or boxwood; or the mouth is of a large size and the edge of the teeth is long, and long one thumb and a half; and between these two thumbs there are two joints of this same fist, which are closed in one and the other, half a thumb long or more; and these two joints are supported in the mouth of the marrow to open when the two thumbs are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, as in the nails; and has two joints of this kind, as you see, of a palm’s length, and two of a large size; and when you see the marrow opening with all the instruments, if you see the woman sitting, the pieces above and the legs below, then rejoin the two joints together in the marrow, and hold the chief of the instruments between her thighs; then close your hand over all the instruments, as if you had made the nails even, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the marrow, until the dance makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very burdensome, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one sees them appear, the work hastens, and the houses are more numerous than before.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If one does not despair of the instrument that has not appeared, for its need is not to be excused.</start_of_turn>
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second toe is retained during infancy, if you command the patient to retain her heel, and then make her cough up the condyle, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she jumps for that, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not happen, if I take a pot and make a perforation or cut, and put herbs in that can open the mouth of the disease, such as rue, chamomile, camomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled or put into boiling water over the fire; then put a sponge or perforation in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the disease, and hold it until vapor comes out of the disease; then make her cough up, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second limb is affected by the disease.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not forced, as it is commanded at the dance, she should moisten her left hand with olive oil or with massage of elevation, and then put it back in its place, and desire the second; and when she has found it, if she grasps and extends it back and forth, so that the mark does not bleed; but she must move it slightly to the side and to the left, and then treat. If it comes and disappears.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mark of the wound is seen, as we have said in the previous treatment, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not of all that we have said, so keep that you do not use for treatment; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the wound, that you bind it to the woman's hip, and then cauterize with oil of thyme; if she will hold it and return, and will come out forced; however, whenever she bears it, if there comes a bad smell from the stomach and the head, and the patient bleaches.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, indeed, to perform fumigations, take heed: neither of the ancients has ever experienced fumigation with rue herbs and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at the time of her menses and of the second stage is thus: ...
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is seen like a dog, and one sets the head in the middle, and the arms wide over the fire; and let the fumigations rise over the charcoal, and the smoke until it is consumed, and do it again.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	No child is born without having perceived the foundation, for it is stamped upon them secretly: if you wish to restore it, do not prick the sensitive part at its root, and do not prick too deeply, and keep the dressing so that it does not touch; then put on soft linen soaked in wine and oil, and then treat the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will stay in place, if you put or pull out a splinter of lead, leave the hands still for a while, and keep the limb still as long as the patient sees the fever rise in bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Never comes this time from the stamping of wounds or incisions; if you must cover that stamping: if it be cured, as we have said of the splinter of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from its foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodulations, and those that come from above the foundation are protrusions, or in between these two parts, if there is a fistula or several; and when the nodulation is old, if it is delayed, and is accompanied by moisture or white or soft pus, and never are these fistulas harmless; they are known by the patient's vomiting or diarrhea when the patient makes an egestion, and by chance when one jumps up.</start_of_turn
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate as far as the bladder, and halfway up the thigh; and reach as far as the joint of the hip, and even to the coccyx bone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows of the fistula that persists at the base, and does not go away; and it is only when you bite down your thumb or the base, that a fine needle of spider or iron enters the fistula when there is no swelling.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is swelling, if you attempt to pull out a fine sponge or hair as long as you feel the attempt or the hair at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there is no sign of pus discharge or vomiting, as we have said: evacuate the wound that it does not burst; if you are hasty to cure.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is made through to the bladder or the urine tube, if in a leap the urine escapes, and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the hip joint, if the attempt of the vein goes down to the limb; if there is no swelling and the pain is not intense, if it has already subsided, and there is no other medicine or support with oil; and in these persistent fistulas there is no remedy except toil, and the folly of the fools who are involved.</start_of_turn>
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that where neither youth nor age is present, hope for health by means of fire, as I have seen; and that the patient lies between your hands upon his back; and let the legs rest as far as up to the thighs, and have the thighs inclined towards the belly; then stretch out the arm, or draw in the loin if there is pain, until you feel the pain cease or the stretching comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the root of the limb, if you must bite your thumb index, if you feel that the stretching has been perceived; and either uncover the bone or feel between the thumb and the index finger, if there is pain, stop when it is certain; for otherwise you will not be able to heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can cure many things without difficulty, but this is not the case; and what helps is to apply the cautery skillfully according to the size of the fistula, as it is said before; and to leave the surrounding tissue around the fistula until the root is reached; and do this two or three times until you feel that these threads that need to be cauterized are burned, which are similar to a bundle of hair; and then close with soft stitches, until the thread is strong, and then close with oil and bandage.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is sound, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is sound, that is good; for if he attempts between and does not pierce until he reaches what is deep, and between your thumb and the attempt a thick covering of hair or fat, and you see the fistula at that which sustains the covering like a wound; if you grasp the start of the fistula and hold it steady before the attempt, and after the burn, as long as it comes up to the head of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and he will recover; then remove those hairs that seem like a bundle of hair, and there will remain nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If he will not move, and if there is a wound between you and the work, if the fire cautery or medical potion is rough.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the blistering of these hairs that grow, the extraction of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of soft swellings that are burned or broiled, until they leak pus, and is the dry medicine.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the thumb or root of the bone is grasped or pulled out, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
