Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the attempt, and between two is the thread or the flesh or bone, or it is close to piercing, if there is no other escape but the passage of a betrothed woman and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you apply pressure until it is healed, or if you wish, you do so as soon as you sense the attempt and cure as before; and do not go too far into the wound, that you do not cover the tenant who holds the foundation, and bring out the discharge in the natural order; then cure it as we have said; by chance if it is healed, or you remove the covering and the mud then when it is peeled off from the foundation, or by attempt or by another pointed instrument; then bind up the wound that is in the wound, as you wish; and study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the posterior part of the foundation: if it is less severe for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either cost or deeply embedded below the skin, take an attempt pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you see that the thread is torn in two, and the attempt is at the root of the fistula until it is at the head
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either cost or deeply embedded below the skin, take an attempt pierced at the head according to this form: if it is pierced in the margin of the foundation downwards, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your root or foundation; and pull out the head of the thread, and join the two ends together, and strain one against the other, and leave it one or two; and do not restrain at any time, until the thread holds these hairs that are between the two, and cease to bleed; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, if you force it to burst in every way you can, it will not be too deeply seated.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suffice to make the opening wide by force, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is sound
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny thumb which we make the fistula is if it is moist and of one part and trenchant; and on the other hand not, for it is not to be held too tightly, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes sont selonc deux manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racine; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you command that I bind according to this manner: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through the hole and pierce the needle through again, and twist two threads of the thread around the needle, and if it is thick; restrain the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and secure everything else, and leave one to correct the excess blood; then put on the foundation a bandage soaked in rose oil or cerate, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it stops bleeding, and when it stops bleeding, if there are other treatments for the wound, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when it is completely dry or firm
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There is often dryness of the bowels in this disease, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you command that you stick to the point of a spatula or your nail the scale under, which does not allow it to moisten; then treat it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it cannot be healed, if you renew the scraping stronger than before, until it breaks through, and is scraped away; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	indeed
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small mark that appears before the limb, and goes out from under the skin; and never does it cause pain, and it is felt as if dead weight, and comes throughout the limb, and more so than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a bundle of rue (or the gut of a vulture) of the size of a thumb, or the size of a barleycorn, and put that bundle on the wound, until the circle of the wound has turned blue; then draw your hand back with all your might until you have pulled out the wound entirely, and put it out from under the skin, and scrape the wound out from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that he does this with a spider or a nail according to this form, and be discreet and restrain him from below:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see that he does this with a spider or a nail according to this form, and be discreet and restrain him from below, do not notice, for must hold still, and must press. And if you see that he does this, if he bites forward or during the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of this form.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a cautery of silver or gold, or of a melted spider or flea; and never make of these small and great instruments except as they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the cure of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	They are small both in chest and belly, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a swelling or the belly is tied up, if you see, and the shoulder is dislocated either forward or backward; and there are two holes in one side, and one in the other; or if the belly or the abdomen has medicines in a bladder or parchment, or if there are several holes throughout, put between each hole one finger’s breadth; then put in this hole one strong thread of gut twisted in an X or hooked around like this; and assemble the belly as if it were a needle. And when the medicine is in, if the loop has the instrument in front of a strong thread, then clip it; and that is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let neither the medicine be too hot nor too cold; anoint the head of the blister with oil or balm of egg, or something similar; then bind it lightly; then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is all white, then draw out the blister, and leave the patient his legs uncovered, and if the medicine sees that it is sufficient, if it has lasted as long as it can; and if he sleeps through the night, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clip the vein in the case of a wound of the belly, and the physician hastens to go out, if it starts again as long as it is harmless.</start_of_turn
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is swelling or inflammation at the base of the blister, or an abscess, if the blister is as soft as for one child; this is the form of a soft blister that sits on the skin, which is strained:
des plaies	and thus is the shape of a subtle blister that appears when the skin is stretched:
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	and thus is the shape of a subtle blister that appears when the skin is stretched: when the skin is stretched, a subtle blister will form. We have already mentioned the cure for wounds; or you may say the cure for hands and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what causes them and depending on the place or the wounds are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things that cause wounds are bites of stone, and the size of spear and nail, or lance or fist or knife, or similar things; or that are done according to the laws of custom, as for example a wound that bites on the cheek, or on the head, or the ear, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for a simple wound, and we will begin with the wounds of the head alone, for the memory will come back to us in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a wound or from something else, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt about the wound itself: if you do this, the patient will recover more quickly from the head downwards even if there is blood from the wound; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction to the diseased part; and listen to the patient’s appetite for wine and solid food.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not recover, if he is without appetite for meat, and does not drink wine, does not eat cheese; and remove the wound, if there is post-traumatic swelling, apply moist lint soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no post-traumatic swelling, if put on the wound when it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by wind, dust, or anything else, I will tell you about that later; and if it has been moved, put on some ointments until it is healed
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a nail and some, and the limbs do not stick together by themselves, if you join them together by stitching, as I will tell you about wounds of the belly, of stitching.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and is painful, and cannot be held together by anything, then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as meat and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or split skin due to decay, and it does not touch the bone, if you can hold it together, and bleed profusely, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicines, if you can stop the artery, and if you find it dislocated, if you can bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a minor cure: put on this powder which makes them adhere as well as when they were moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind them together finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins together all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it to drain, if it does not swell; for we do not set the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we perform this treatment alone, when we do not have the incense or blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved, even if it is still fresh, do not put on this powder; but put on some unguents that digest, or poultices of ground barley made with water and honey, until it has bled enough; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a fracture accompanies the wound, and it is small, if you grasp it with fine tweezers; I will tell you later about greater fractures.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the skull, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If the nerve is exposed, if there is no other injury except to leave the wound open, and do not put on any restraining dressing, because it hinders the nerve and makes it retract; do not put anything rough on the wound, because the substance of the nerve is cold, and the continuation of the pain is with the marrow, which is the most painful limb; but if the medicine is soft, like boiled chalk in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and poppy seeds boiled in sweet water, and other similar things, and moist unguents.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the bone and surrounding tissue are split, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If wounds are deep and swollen, and there is swelling from the base; if an artery is severed, blood flows freely; if the bone is fractured, and marrow and cautery mingle; if the cartilage of the jaw is fractured, or the nails of the fingers and toes are fractured, the hand must be held still, for the meat hangs loose if the nail is broken above the jaw; do not touch the jaw but restore it to its natural position; then stretch the limb slowly and leave it for a while; then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; if the wound has made an imprint in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments must be pulled out, do not attempt to extract anything that you cannot grasp; leave as much as possible of the wound exposed and aligned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, if the cure is as I have said in the chapter.</start_of_turn
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or a knife.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if you see that the wound is open to the wind, do not allow the patient to move: the wound is mortal; if it is not deep and is fresh throughout, if you do not put in the first hour the powder, do not bind it up with the wound that it does not cause him further pain or depth; return to the body and comfort the patient; but put in an astringent, and bind it twice; if there is no astringent, put into the wound some fine cotton to absorb the moisture, and make the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four or more; if there is no spasm, do not move the body or strain the wound. When you see the bones in their place, do not pull out the wound.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tension of the tendons and other cures, as long as it is sane; and if it cannot be cured, and if it is necessary, perform an incision to remove the abscess; if the cure is to be made thus.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision of a spear or knife, and it is simple, or worse at the front or back, if the treatment of what is before is necessary; if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, if you desire the wound, and the blood vessels if they are severed; and if they are not severed, if you leave the wound open, if it aligns the extractions; and for other wounds, as for other members, the judge shall decide as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	thus other wounds will also judge him as we have said.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The belly is greatly and meanly swollen and slightly so; a great wound never comes upon the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, by which the intestines are drawn inwards; and the ribs are more painful, and never worth more than a small wound than a great one, forasmuch as one must return the intestines more often than once; forasmuch as the intestines swell up so much that they feel the fruit, if they return more often, it is better for the lesser wound; thus it is better to leave the intestines in their place than to draw them out. The intestines are usually evacuated in three ways: two common ribs arise in the belly rib, and the ribs of the other wounds from the ribs and two other ribs are common to other wounds; and all of them are more common with the belly rib, and I will speak of it and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is pressing, and only a little thing is protruding, this can be remedied in two ways: either by the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the area somewhat: moisten a sponge or I put a wet drape over it simply, or you can burn in vinegar scraping and pinching and spiking, and raise the intestine until it is firm; and do not at any time make this movement restrictive, and be quiet that you do not cause it to swell further.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see swelling depart, if the intestine is wet or elevated and bad, because by this is the entry to something; and if it cannot enter, if there is a wound in the place, with the instrument we can compress the swellings; and the first treatment is quiet that the size, that we must not cut excessively without need, for it is the instrument for cutting: if we cut too deeply in the curve and it slips not, and once cut like this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines protrude, if you stop the bleeding according to its natural form in its own place, if you have been negligent, for this is worth as much as a mistake.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is at the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient lying on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is at the lower part of the belly, put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts, and in the same way if the belly is split into two parts, put the hand on the side that is higher than the other; and thus you must manage what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put on what has appeared between the hands, and keep all the edges together; this is the common method of stitching and is to take a needle or more according to the quantity of the wound, then leave the edges of the wound at a distance, and pierce the two holes in the skin with the two holes in the siphac, which is under the skin, as much as you make it pierce through that part, and reunite the two edges of the siphac together; then strain a double thread around the needle from two parts, then reunite the two edges of the wound in order, and then leave a distance, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this until the wound is completely restricted; and let the needles be neither too fine nor too thick, for the fine needles cover all the substance, and the thick ones do not penetrate well: for this reason it is necessary that they be neither too fine nor too thick; and do not force the needles too much against the substance and the skin, as they do not cover and open the wound before the suture; and then join the holes of the needles, that they do not bruise the patient at night, and put on bands or patches on the holes of the needles in order to hold, and leave them as long as the wound is sutured; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only one or two stitches in the second stitching that is common, and that you reunite the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the siphac together with one needle or there is one strong thread in the middle. And when you have pierced these two holes together, reunite the needle at the part where you began, in the manner that we cut the threads. And leave a distance between each stitch equal to the thickness of a minor finger; this stitch is useful for a home, and I stitched a wound once upon a time on the side of the breast, which was caused by a knife, and the wound was more than half a palm in size, and there were intestines well two palms in size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I shall return the intestine when it has been out for XXIV hours, and the wound has healed for xv days; the treatment was successful and the patient is well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the patient had lost hope that he would recover, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with medicine, for I was in the land of Israel where there is no doctor, no medicine; and I did nothing more for the wound except to change the dressing twice a day, and to apply honey until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you may say two ways to stitch: take the needle and pass it through from the underside until it reaches the midpoint; when it has grasped the right edge, if the needle slips or tears or you have passed the needle, and you must pierce again from the underside until you reach the underside; and you will understand this stitching as well as a leatherworker does when he sews pelts, and that you leave once the hair has passed over, and you take it back again, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of dressing, which Galiens does most frequently, if it is so that no one else does it, which assembles the two parts naturally, and joins one of the heads to the other head, in part like this: pierce a needle or head of a pin near the adjacent head, and make the former one bleed only, and leave the two heads of the pin; then withdraw the needle, and make it bleed from the lower part until it reaches this far, with two heads of the pin; then make it bleed from one and the other from the lower part until it reaches this far, with two other pins that are on the other side; and this is the wisest method of dressing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says that no one testifies to this; we must sew up the belly with two needles, or there must be yarn in the navel; and we must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew up wounds; and stitches that when the wound has returned to its former state, if the suture is stronger than the other wounds of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you reattach the intestines and gut, then put on the dusting powder; if it has moved, do not put on any dressing that is present until the wound has healed; then tighten the thread, and be careful of the edges, the corners, and the surrounding area; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on nothing but vinegar and oil until it starts to ooze blood.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You do not need any other medicine for many wounds except for those that are serious; and if you doubt whether the wound is making common progress as the principal members, you must cover it with coarse linen soaked in warm oil of poppies, or rose oil, and put it on the wound; and wash the surrounding area. If there is pain or gangrene in the bowels, and this happens many times, if the black vomit is dark brown, and even if the gangrene reaches the intestines; pierce through it, and drain out the contents when the large intestines are more easily healed than the small intestines.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot recover when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the pulse leaps from the wound, if it returns backward just as the intestine; while it is fresh; and if it is pale and becomes black or dark, if you must tie the black part, for there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the bone, and hang the two heads down from the lower part of the wound until the pulse has disappeared, and the wound will be healed.
de la routure dou boueil	because of the pain of the burn
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it in small steps, because I have seen that one bone has been swollen or pierced by a lance; and the wound was at the side of the stomach, and became filled and formed a fistula, and in this there was vomiting and diarrhea; I treated it as I could, and I did not cease to subtilize until it was healed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but there was no harm, but many provisions, and food and drink; and they say that whenever there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligatured in parts. Take tweezers of great size, then assemble the layers of the wound, and when the tweezers have passed over the opening, if you put two layers over it, if it strains its opening over; and then press the testicles, and this is held if it cannot be released, then put another suture afterwards in that manner that before, until the wound is whole.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the gut is perforated, and there is no other inconvenience to the patient, and it can be ligated with a fine thread that is cut from the gut itself, in parts. Take the head of this gut thread that is outside, and then tie the head of this gut thread to the head of this fine thread, and pass the thread through the needle, and sew up the gut, and hold it in place; and this method of stitching with tweezers is not fierce except according to the condition and the hope; and if the wound is great and wide, like that which is in one of the large intestines, if there is no other remedy, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds and incisions, whenever they burst, if they are called universally 'fistula', and even when they are sewn and rent bow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	When a wound or incision bursts, if it is universally called 'fistula', and even when it is sewn and rent bow. And fistula is according to truth a nodulation that needs to be strong and white, or one does not feel pain; and it is as much sewn as the quill of a bird; and never in clear liquid, and sometimes thick; never too little, and sometimes enough; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not cured, and there is no pus, is only by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or the hardness of the flesh; or by its malice; or because there is hardness deep down, and on the skin, that does not allow new pus to form; or there is too much liquid; or the bone is twisted, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because corruption is like pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion and late in health, and flees by nature; or there is a vein or bone: and I have already mentioned all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you should know that I will tell you about the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that occur in all limbs with pain; for there are wounds which arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the jaw, or intestines, or bladder, or some of the bones, or the shoulder blade, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and if any part comes to the property of the principal limb, and the rest.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All wounds of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is any wound that does not come to light only as far as I have said, and you have faith in a cure, and you see it approach, if it is straight, if the pain; and if it is crooked, if you can make a slight attempt to pull, for it swells inward towards the crookedness; and if the wound is pierced and you do not well bind it, if it bursts by one of the perforations, for the moisture is short from one perforation to another, and it softens; then the pain suddenly departs from your hand, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and is crushed together, and ask the patient of the pain he feels at the pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you know truly the place or whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or some of those I have told you, if the cure agrees with what I have said, and the bone is forced out of its place and the corrupt humors that are within; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the wound is deeply straight, if you can force it out, as much as you can; and then put soft dressings on the medicine bag, and leave it until the medicine consumes the superfluous that remains at the bottom; and then put on oily dressings that will adhere to the wound until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the wound, if it bursts.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or main principal does not impede you, or if the bone is discovered to have corruption and blackness, if the latter is all bony, then cure it with things that are warming until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and you must go back as before, take out the bones that are not right until you reach the marrow; if you uncover and desire as much as you can until you reach the bottom, and restore the limb; and if it is then healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If it is not thus, if the corruption is too great to bear, you will not be able to go on; if there is no other remedy except to let it run its course; and if there is but a small bone that is corrupted, and you attempt to remove it with pliers, if the bone is covered with something that will prevent its extraction, or if there is more than one bone, if you break them, do not leave one of them behind; and if moisture opposes you, and there is neither doubt nor fear, then embrace moisture and warmth and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If thou dost not drive out the poison at an hour, put upon the wound some substance that doth hinder corruption, and leave it until the wound doth lie settled upon the bones; then it will be lighter concerning the bones. And if it be a great bone, as a limb or thigh, thou must only slightly restrain the corruption until the marrow be wholly ossified, and then restore the wound. And if there be much of the bone corrupted, come down to the marrow; if thou dost cover it and cover all until the corruption be gone, and then cure it until it be healed. And I tell thee of a fistula which I saw in a man’s limb, that thou mayest take example thereby and help in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years of age who had a pain in his leg due to something within the bone, so that the matter came out of his leg; and he had a large abscess, but he did not know what caused it. But he was so foolish that he did more harm than good by opening the abscess too wide and corrupting a great deal of matter, and made a fistula, and there came out much pus that all the bones groaned and the matter was softened; and he remained lame for two years, and there was no skill in his hands, as far as I know, except that which I saw him use of his medicines, and that which cured him of the abscesses that occurred from the great bones; and his leg and medicines became red, and his bones had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound one of these holes, then circled all the holes, and found that one followed the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I bound one of these holes and found part of the bone broken, corrupt and putrefying, extending to the innermost part of the bone; I extracted what appeared to be a fragment of the fractured bone, and I considered that there was no further corruption except for that which I had already seen; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, without being able to join [the bone fragments]; then I began again, and once more I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I extracted it, and then I rejoined it, and I thought I would try to join the bone; but I could only do so as long as I could grasp a palm of the bone, and when I had grasped it for all its might, I restored it with medicines; and it healed soundly and without further fracture, except for the faintness of the patient, who could not bear the pain, and for the fear of death which I had avoided for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is there bloodletting in this work, but the patient remained whole; and from the bone there grew a hard scale, and it was in good condition and caused neither pain nor discomfort in any way, neither from the start nor afterwards.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no part of the limb, if you wish to bind it in this manner: take one thread and strain it at the head of the bone that is open, and command no one to extend it upwards; and put another thread of linen more coarse than the first, and bind it above the scale that is now departing from the bone, and extend the head, so that you tear the corrupt scale from the socket, and uncover the scale above the limb where you see it bound; and put in place a plug or a piece of lead to cover the corrupt scale; and bind as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bind again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and does not open by itself, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, uncover the marrow all around; then put on a pair of gloves and with one hand stretch out the corruption from the other; and if the corruption is at the joint, join the corrupted joint and stretch out the bone or what is in it from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other vessel but the marrow; and if the corruption is in the wrist or in the elbow, if it is strong in that matter, but whatever it is, it must be enquired about that corrosion, how it opened; and the surrounding parts must be examined in all ways, except for the vein or nerve; and that the incision and the sutures should cover these bones many times, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of swelling, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it is necessary to make a similar imitation of the work of this instrument; and the work will show you the instrument that you must have, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the methods of diseases; if you are in doubt about the instrument that you must have according to this, it must be doubted.
dou feu	If you think the instrument which you must use is appropriate according to this, then use it.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder may be dislocated by injury, swelling, or fever. When you have treated the underlying cause with medicine, but it has not helped, if you cover the limb until the cause has passed, the patient may escape death by this means or by the greater malice of the default of the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire, and afterward there follows a swelling of the limb, taking in all its substance; if you are hasty in covering it, and if it is by the percussion of some venomous creatures, as for example, scorpions of the sea and vipers, and the like, if the corrosion is at the root of the bone, if you do not give it space to come out until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes to the hand, if the cope is at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cope is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and nothing but the quantity of its virtue is of any use; and do all that you can when the corrosion comes or leaves: if it comes in the first joint, if the cope afterwards comes in the second joint; and if it comes or leaves, if you cope all that is above; and if it goes up to the leg, if you cope at the knee; and if it comes below the knee, if there is nothing else to do but leave the patient to die; and you should bandage the limb if you tie it below and above, and stretch out one minister at the lower ligament and another minister at the upper ligament, and you should dissect the tissue between the two ligaments at one spatulate wide, until the bone is exposed; then cope or remove the drape, and put some lint in the part where the drape was, so that the silk does not touch the sound limb, and come to the patient another wound and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when working, if you cauterize the limb excessively, or put on restrictive powders; then return to your medicine until it is accompanied; then bind the limb securely with a suitable bandage, and treat until healed; and I will tell you of a case in which this happened: there was a blackness that seemed to burn the flesh, and that corruption began at the root of the limb, as far as it could; and when we saw the corruption, if we did not cover the limb, it healed; and when we later saw the corruption return at the root of the limb, we applied things that would impede the corruption, but it continued; and I had to cut off the limb, as I had no hope of saving it; and I feared that if I did not amputate, it would die, for the strength of the limb was weak; and he awoke, and returned to his home, and when he came back he covered his limb, and it healed; and I have never heard of anything like it except in this case, when we were forced to do it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes an abscess in the flesh that does not linger for a long time, making great swelling; then it bursts and ruptures, and in leaping up it tears the flesh, and lingers there like a vessel; and the skin which is under it is just as thin as a silken cloth, and does not adhere to the bone or the nerve, and such an ailment is called “sain,” and is not called “fistula”; but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone embedded in the flesh, it is called “fistula”; and if the skin is split from that point, and even when it is thin like a silken cloth, it does not recover.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the skin is loosened and corruption does not lie deep within, and the skin is thick like flesh, if the surgeon grasps the testicles: look if the swelling is great and the swelling which is in it has a foul odor, then make a plaster of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take alum, oil, and alum, equally, and mix the plaster with these ingredients until it is as thick as honey; then take some of this plaster according to your need, and make it hot and thick, and administer it to the affected area; strain the excess. Repeat this treatment until the swelling is reduced and the pain is gone; do not administer plaster of alum with vinegar, except when this medicine is not present. Take vinegar of pomegranate and vomit, then let it drain, and administer plaster until you feel that the swelling has gone down; if the patient cannot bear the pain, neither the Egyptian plaster nor the vinegar, if you give vinegar and honey plaster or if there is a little bit of alum in it; or make plaster of honey and wine, because honey has the power to soften and cleanse, and the wine will make the wound dry. When you have done this, and you are confident that the swelling has gone down, if there is any purulent discharge in the testicles, and you take bandage plaster, make it with oil of rose and wine; or make plaster from other medicines and unguents, of which I have spoken of their properties or treatment of unguents; and if the wound is too wide, if the thumb and index finger leave so much space that the plaster will not enter, if the thumb has been burned or if it is swollen, put in a pad of Egyptian unguent or balsam, until it is swollen; if the wound is too large, if the thumb and index finger leave so little space that the plaster will enter, and if there is purulent discharge coming from below the thumb, if the thumb has been grasped or is lower than it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the arm hangs down, if you do not leave some hanging hair; if you do not cover the hair at the roots as you see, it will appear in such a way that the arm hangs lower than before. For when the arm hangs down, if you do not leave some hanging hair and you do not cover the hair at the roots as you see, it will appear in this way: the arm hangs loosely downward, and you must leave nothing of the arm hanging; then take consolidating medicines to bring back the blood, and cover with a linen cloth that covers the whole wound; then put force where the skin has been cut, which will be wider than before, because there are sutures upon the other cloth according to the quantity of the cut, and put the sutures on the wound in such a way as to align the arm, and do not remove the large cloth until after one time; and whoever has been cut from the skin will often remove the sutures to align the arm, and will wipe away what is hanging from the arm, if that is venom or blood or sufficient, or digested or indigested; take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine is in this way extended and you see the nature of the jump on the wound, if the blood has already clotted, and approach the health. Then untie the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, if you see the other cloth, renew the sutures.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the limb suddenly feels sick after remaining still for a while, it is likely that the swelling has become excessive.</start_of_turn>
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison comes after a long tension, if you do not rouse yourself from sleep, because the sickness approaches.
