Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if subtle poison comes after a long tension, if you do not rouse yourself from sleep, because the sickness approaches. For there are some who delay their ailments in their wounds, and others do the opposite; and if you become unwell after prolonged fasting, your veins do not swell. If your veins are late in swelling, and are swollen, if there are any moist and dry medicines, as diaphel, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, which is the last medicine; take diaphel and mix it with rose oil and the juice of a hundred wines equal in quantity; then confect and use. This itself makes honey swell, when diaphel is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them up, and sprinkle them on honey when it is taken off the fire; then glue on a bandage and take it off the chest, and do not administer an aristologist for a long time, or celestial roots, which is as much like flour sometimes and sometimes like hundredweight; and use simple or compound. Grind them up, make powder, and sprinkle it on honey as I have said, and use. And if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then it is because the corruption has spread throughout the body, and has made an imprint on the bone, or has hardened the limbs, or caused inflammation. If the cure for fistula is taken, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the gland.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that originates from the swelling of the pouch of the hand, or the pit, or by chance originates in other two places; and when it is inflamed, and no care is taken, if it comes to an abscess of the thumb, it swells and bursts as much as it can until it reaches the root of the thumb, and by chance it swells all the way; and there comes the corrosion up to the bone, until there is sharp pain, and the head of the thumb is large, and the colour is dark brown.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have cured it as we have said in the division, and the cure has not profited, if you must do so, cut away all the superfluous tissue that remains from the thumb, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help when the bone is sound, and the thumb is flexible; and if the thumb presses on the wound, and starts to bleed, if you must do so, remove all but a little of the callous from the thumb itself, leaving the rest above, and remove the callous little by little, and put on medicines that are astringent and corrosive to remove everything; then keep the wound clean until it is healed
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the bone is corroded, if it cracks and breaks, for as much as the corrupted bone is, it cannot be healed; and if you see that the thumb is corrupted, if it cracks from the nail downwards as it is said above, then you must cure it until it is healed. And if it is inflamed, swollen, and causes great pain, it is best that you first heal it; then break the bone at the tip of the thumb by cutting across just below the nail, and keep the size from going further than the nail itself, for the patient would feel too great pain; and if that happens, put something over which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the hand must be great.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two thumbs that are born in the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is part where there is bone, and never nail, and none are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in the flesh of the hand itself.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in no new doubt does not move; he who is born at the joint of the elbow, by chance moves; the size of him who is fleshed is slight, in part like this: size as in the root of a broad spindle.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the joint is grief to cure: if you hold it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	He who is born or must later without doubt, if you must, first close the flesh completely around the bone until it is level, then close the bone to a convenient distance from this one, then cure it until it is sound
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come about must be reassembled either by birth, or by healing of a wound, or by fire cautery, or by like things.</start_of_turn
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you must close the wound, if it must be repaired according to its natural form; then put between two stitches or cloths soaked in rose oil, that they do not adhere; or you put between two pieces of soft lead, until it is healed, as it must be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When they adhere to neither side with the palm, if they adhere too tightly.</start_of_turn
des vils	des vils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are great vessels enclosed with black bile, which comes in greater quantity in members that are tormented by pain and that are in motion and labor, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not administer any purgatives of col, and then the remainder of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of fire is in two ways: one is with sponges, and we force out the black bile; the other method is if you ligate the vein and force out all the blood.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first raise the affected limb high and warm it until the great vessel does not appear slippery; then strain the limb of the patient from under the hip down to the heel; then cut the vein in one, two or three places, of a large size, and ligate and force out the black bile from your hand from the head to the heel, until as much blood has come out as the patient can tolerate; and then tie it off and command him to eat nourishing food; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.</start_of_turn
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient lies down. If there is hair, remove it. Then bathe or wash the limb with warm water until it turns red. Swelling will follow. If you have no bath, burn the limb with fire and then place the thumb over the long bone of the elbow or the lower part of the calf; then bind the skin around the joint, and gently stretch the limb until it feels taut; it will turn red and black. Then release the thumb when the limb is relaxed. Then bind again, and do so three times. Then bind the skin over the joint until it feels taut. Then release the thumb once more. Then bind again as before. Continue this process until the limb is completely healed. If you are unable to draw out the hair and it remains entangled, grasp it firmly with a strong needle and remove it. Then bandage the limb tightly on both sides.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If the eye is contracted, torted, and surrounded together, and is not straight, as we have said, then you must make an opening in it, but do not cover it; and take it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	If the eye is curved like a bow, and is not pierced, but is of great curvature, for if it were slight, it would close the vein, but make it large as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of a civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth or where there is no moisture; and by chance it appears elsewhere except in the limb, and this comes from the putrefaction that comes from the decay of the leather, as it comes from inside the serpent’s body and outwards, enclosing between skin and flesh
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	If there are signs of the beginning of this vein, that is, if there is a great swelling in the limb, then it is chained at the root, and the vein bursts forth like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the opening is made, if it is thought that the piece of sponge should be wrapped around for one and a half inches, and the knot, and that the sponge should be left in the limb, and every time that there is a point of pain, if the wrapping is around the sponge and the knot, and the swelling; and if it is too long, if one end is cut off, and the other is wrapped around, and is not covered in its root, until it is all gone; for if you cover it, if it returns into the flesh, it brings about positing and putrefaction or death, and makes the disease worse; therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and thoroughly until it is cured, and that nothing be left in or on it; and there has never been a case in which this vein has been treated with five palms of sponge, or ten, and one has not died from it, since it has been done with ten palms of sponge. When it is covered, if there is one or two veins or an opening, and the hole is made right through, if everything is gone; and the matter that is inside is to be evacuated, and medicines that promote healing should be administered without any delay, and the wound should be cured like the apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it bursts at the shoulder joint, or on the shoulder, and blood spurts out; cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it bursts at the shoulder joint, or on the shoulder, and blood spurts out; cure it as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease," because it often causes swelling of the lymph nodes, and is a small vein that originates between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, ascending and descending, and the patient feels it well throughout the limbs, as far as the skin is taut or the veins burst, and spur; and it is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as bile, worms, and feces or the like. There is doubt of its severity, for when it runs through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes out on the surface, by chance it returns, and destroys the fat. This often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not go away until it has gone, then you must bind the limb above and below with a strong tie, and then press above and pull down, and if it does not come out, if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greater harm that it makes is if it breaks the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, then strain from it the hair that grows under the nail, then press above and pull down; and you must use the patient of purgatives of solid medicines for the bad humors that are carried, and let him eat nourishing foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if it will not go away until it has gone, then you must bind the limb above and below with a strong tie, and then press above and pull down, and if it does not come out, if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies; and the greater harm that it makes is if it breaks the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, then strain from it the hair that grows under the nail, then press above and pull down; and you must use the patient of purgatives of solid medicines for the bad humors that are carried, and let him eat nourishing foods.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land 'vakirir', and is a pain that comes in successive parts of the body; and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I went to see a sick woman, and discovered swellings on her arms, and saw a small swelling in her groin; and afterwards, I saw it rise up like a worm on the shoulder, more stretched out than anything, as much as if there were gold in the limb when it was struck against another; the pain departed from that limb and settled in the shoulder, and then afterwards subsided throughout the limb, until it came to the other arm; and she told me that it often turned back into the limb.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered what he meant by that, because I had never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I do not want to say that because of the pain in the limb there is no movement of limbs; but I do not believe it, for I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had dry bones and exposed veins, and because of that appeared that constraint; and I do not see it according to this reason those things which are delicious, and which have moist bones and veins restored
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see this disease cured, and the patient feels the pain, if the joint above and below has become inflamed, then immediately support the limb as much as the constraint of the wound allows; and cauterize the limb. If you do not see movement at your eyes, if the cure has driven out the swelling, like foul pills, and serpin pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	When you see this disease cured, and the patient feels the pain, if the joint above and below has become inflamed, then immediately support the limb as much as the constraint of the wound allows; and cauterize the limb. If you do not see movement at your eyes, if the cure has driven out the swelling, like foul pills, and serpin pills, and similar things.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are varied, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they cause.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of these boils is such that some have large points, some have small points, some have hairs, and some have pus; and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces; and those that break in no limb break in two ways: either in the principal limb, like the brain, arm, liver, kidney, spleen, intestine, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the limb is fractured in no part of its bones, and the sign of death is shown, which I will tell you later, you will learn: if you hesitate to extract this arrow, for many more will follow; and when this bad sign appears, do not learn me, for the arrow is not yet withdrawn, if you dare, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of madness when the arrow pierces the bone and leaps the marrow that is above the brain, is when scooping and sode and vomiting and spitting and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixing of senses, and vomiting of bile; and by chance it is without noise of nose or ears; or by chance it loses speech and voice; and leaps from the wound a white moistor resembling pus, and in leaping like burnt hair; and if this sign teaches you, if you stay away from the cure, take out the arrow if it is not already gone.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a fracture when it breaks or cracks are that it is close to the left breastbone and feels as though it were stuck in something hard, without any visible wound; and by chance the fracture moves like a chicken, and in dark blood without, and comes with chills and cold sweat, and fainting: it is certain that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that never heals is only without pus coming from the wound, and the swelling increases, and the patient’s complexion changes, and he sighs deeply and vomits profusely.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow tip remains in the covering of the wound, if it is removed, there is great pain and swelling, and deep sighing; and the limb moves abnormally
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrow tip is broken or in the stomach, by chance no sign of indigestible meat from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow tip is broken or in the stomach, and there is no sign of feces in the intestines, if there is no hope for recovery, do not attempt to extract the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the bladder stone passes into the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if it is fractured and the collarbone and the jaw and the shoulder and the elbow and the wrist and the forearm and the leg, and the like, is only saved by numerous precautions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the bladder stone is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have told you before, for in this case you must do something else.</start_of_turn>
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There was in my house a splinter which had fallen or slipped into the root of the ear: I grasped it, and it slipped from the other side of the earlobe, and was cured without any damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And it happened in a game that a splinter had fallen into the oil of the ear from the papilla of the ear, and the splinter was returned, and did not touch anything except the tip towards the back; and the splinter was as large as a Turkish arch, and at all that was heard was a slight sound in the ear; the game was cured, and there was no further mishap
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And bring out an arrow from the throat to a cresting, and the Arab physicians said: I saw the tonsils, and I grasped them as long as I could, and it was healed the cresting.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled out an arrow from the chest, which was in the belly, and I thought it would die; but after it had passed XXX days, if it did not mend its disposition; I cut on the arrow, and I bound it, and I pulled it out, and there was no bad consequence.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has an arrow stuck in his chest or back, and the wound is deep; and when I pulled out the arrow from within, I did not bind its disposition, and I found no discomfort in any of its natural works
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And as for another man, who had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was deep; and when I pulled out the arrow he suffered great pain; and there were many similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And remove an arrow from the king's arm, which was stuck in the middle of the shoulder, and was declining to the outer side; and the arrow was completely extracted. I came to attend to the cure afterwards when it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very sore.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would try to treat it with all my skill, and I did not feel any pain; and there was no tingling or pain in the outer ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was the tip of the arrow. I put on an absorbent dressing around the wound, in order that it would not swell; and the arrow came out by itself
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I kept the dressing on for several days, and I closed the wound; and when I saw the patient again I found that the arrow was still in his shoulder; and he told me about it
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed above the wound the corrosive medicine of vinegar by hand for days, until it was softened; I then tried to remove it, and I felt the head of the splinter which was breaking at the root; then I applied the vinegar again to the opening of the wound until the head of the splinter appeared visibly; and it passed out well at the end of the second month, and then it grew so large that I could not remove the nails, and I had to cut it from one side and from the other; and I could not do anything about it. Therefore I continued to undermine and torment it in various ways, until I was able to remove the nails as they were well made, as it is said at the end of this chapter, until I had finished with it, and I restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it anyway, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me what is the quality of the extraction of these arrows, if you put your cure on that which I do not speak of, for the books cannot teach me that; but you know masters better than anyone that which is present and lacking, truly nine works, and nine new instruments, from the descent of the things that come into this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not arise from members or that they are fictious because of two handling: either by the loop or that they enter, or by another; and that which leaps forth by weight or that enters, that is an arrow that has penetrated flesh, and it leaps never more now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it until the flesh is thoroughly corrupted, and rejoice at its issue; and just as if it is fictious in bone, and it cannot be extracted, if you leave it there for some days, and it moves every day; and then it leaps, and if it does not leap, if it pierces through to the marrow of all its bones, until the bones are swollen, and then you pull out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the splinter is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and there are no other accidents which I have mentioned to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even again after some days, for if the splinter comes out whole, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the splinter is fixed only in the bone and does not come out whole, but remains in the bone for some days without any other accident, if the patient experiences pain, do not attempt to pull it out.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is fixed firmly and will not yield, if you administer tarres around it, as I have said; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the splinter is embedded in the bone and cannot be seen, if there is any doubt; and if you grasp it, if it is grasped without a suitable instrument; and if you do not wish to risk the wound, and for the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the wound is large; then remove the splinter as best you can, and if there is any ear attached to it, which is held by two parts of the muscle that you must grasp, and then break or crush the ear of the splinter as much as you can, until you can remove it; and take care that you do not break the splinter, that you remove it more firmly.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it once, if the limb remains bent inward, then grasp it firmly, for the extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If bleeding hinders the treatment, if the wound or abscess demands it, do not hesitate to make an incision of the nerve or vein; and take care that you extract the foreign body without danger, either forward or backward, or twisting or bending; and maintain the patient in the position he was in when the arrow fell into him, for that is the greatest aid of all, and if you cannot do this, follow the signs which he shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes from another place, or if there is no wound, or if the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt: then make the opening as wide as the tweezers can hold it, and then extract it: if it breaks now.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be grasped, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it breaks; if the arrow is full, if it has all its barbs: if it has tears, and you see it is necessary, give an antidote with a hook, so that the tip of the arrow is caught in the hook of the instrument; then pull out the arrow, and if the arrow is hooked, if the instrument has a pointed tip entering the wound, to make the extraction easier.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the bandage is stuck, if you must, grasp all the hair around the wound or the poison is there, if you wish; then cure the wound as it should be cured.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the bandage is torn or broken at the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and is close by, and you must cover it up, if you grasp; and hold the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound, if necessary; and cure as long as it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the nails with which we treat the saiettes are similar to the beak of an oyster, and thus be the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the splinter.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the end of the shoulder is like the wing of a bird, to push back the head of the shoulder, as it is in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the fire never stops pulsating until it is new.
des voinnes dou cors communes	From common veins do blood often flow.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins which we must consider are sixteen in number, that is to say: two veins which are behind the ears, which are covered by the two «herbaches»; and two arteries which are in the two temples which appear; and two veins which are in the two armpits, which are covered by «aspires*/; and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the top of the nose; and the two veins which are at the collar; and the two veins which are under the chin, which are covered by «augeherich»; and two veins which are at the back of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which we commonly handle are five in number in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the elbow, and is called the superficial vein; and the middle one is called the fast, and is composed of the cephalic and brachial veins, and is called the deep vein; and the brachial vein is either on the front or back of the elbow, and is called the radial vein, and is above the olecranon, which is the one we often see on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the ulnar and ring fingers, and if there are two of them; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one which is below the elbow of the left side of the forearm, and the second which is below the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called the sural, which is in the ankle of the other leg; and in the other leg are three veins below these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps as old purges, and to evacuate; and the quality of the blood, as I have said, is that you raise the head of the patient and wipe the hand or the veins are rough; then stretch the patient’s neck with a pin, as long as the two veins behind the ears depend from the head: when the thumb and index finger touch, and you feel the pulse of your thumb, if it signifies an embolism; then take the lancet and pierce through the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand on the whole vein above, and squeeze and the skin and the vein well two must pass through, and make blood spurt until you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmie accustomed, and at the root of the tears of agues as eyes; and the quality of the doctor is such as I have said: and that the patient has strained his neck, as the two veins open wide; and he feels the pulse down to his thumb, and then he signs his mark; then he places his thumb on the vein at the top of his thumb index, and grasps the lancet down, and grasps the vein at the top, and the cope, as he has done in two other veins, and makes correction of the blood according to his necessity; then he releases the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on cotton; and then the swelling forms, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this in relation to its coping and its extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as the blood from the cephalic vein, for there are diseases of the face of old age, such as migraine and redness; and the like if the patient strains his neck by turning, as long as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as the blood from the cephalic vein; for there are diseases of the face of old age, such as migraine and redness. And the like if the patient strains his neck by turning, as long as the vein bursts. Then take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this. Place the point on the vein, and hold with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the quantity that you see. Then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is whole and never more let the work be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, I advise that the flame be neither too great nor too small; and the latter is better, for the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins which are two cubits in length helps to strengthen the eyes, the tongue, the cheeks, the ears in wax, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their blood is that when the patient strains his throat by twisting from side to side, as before; then the same, and either the blood runs black, or a little black, for there is no marrow.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make an opening of the blood, as much as you are able, and then bind it up, and bind it well.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the jaw is worth like water, and has sode forsene, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and the same when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that when the patient strains his throat, he strains his jaw to his left hand, and takes a moderate flame long, and holds it in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open very well in this place, and he must begin to correct it now; and do not go too deep, and make the correction of the blood according to your need, and leave it for one night, because it is easily restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the second pair is useful for the extraction of the spleen, for the beginning of mixing, for the mouth of maladies, for spitting blood, for corrosions, for herpes, for tumors; and the quality of the blood is that the patient grasps his collar with both hands, as we have said; and either the master is standing above the patient’s head, and the patient sits on one seat, then open the vein widely, take out the blood slowly, as much as is necessary; then repeat the process in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and strain the blood moderately, that the patient does not suffocate; and leave it until morning, that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The blood of the second pair is useful for the extraction of the spleen, for the beginning of mixing, for the mouth of maladies, for spitting blood, for corrosions, for herpes, for tumors; and the quality of the blood is that the patient grasps his collar with both hands, as we have said; and either the master is standing above the patient’s head, and the patient sits on one seat, then open the vein widely, take out the blood slowly, as much as is necessary; then repeat the process in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and strain the blood moderately, that the patient does not suffocate; and leave it until morning, that the wound is healed.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins from the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the limbs, and dullness and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And if the quality of the blood be to make the patient sit before thee, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the palm of the hand towards thee, and behold two veins, one on the right side of the hand and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and that there are small veins running alongside them: therefore close both of them; and if thou canst not know them, and if thou art in doubt, if thou close the greatest of the two veins from the wrist downwards, and as much of the two veins as are below and above, for that is the right way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And if the quality of the blood be to make the patient sit before thee, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the palm of the hand towards thee, and behold two veins, one on the right side of the hand and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and that there are small veins running alongside them: therefore close both of them; and if thou canst not know them, and if thou art in doubt, if thou close the greatest of the two veins from the wrist downwards, and as much of the two veins as are below and above, for that is the right way.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins that are above the tongue helps after the blood of the cephalic vein; and this is at the stretching of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the blood is such that if the patient stretches out his hands before the sun, and stretches his tongue, and looks under each rib, he will see a black vein: so both of them are the same, and do not be too quick to pierce, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins which we commonly cauterise are usually bled by two methods: either by pricking with a blunt lancet or with an olive-shaped needle as for cutting trenches, and this is called ‘anesil’; and they are large and olive-shaped according to the size and stretching of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame burning brightly if famous, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it must be known for opening the large veins filled with thick blood, which contain much blood and trouble; and this is the form of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for the healing of the small veins, or where there is little yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments such as hoarseness, swelling in the throat, or pain in the feet or belly; and it is known that it should flow steadily, and that it should abstain from the artery which is beside it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it touches the artery, and blood spurts out, if it is known to be stopped; as I have said; and it must not be grasped too tightly, but cut as cleanly as possible.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basal vein does not open visibly, if you must extract it, and tie another one; or you want no further bloodshed, or you prefer to take in hand the vein which is in the arm: it will open visibly; and grasp it with the flame as we have said
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If thou seest the head of the blood vessel known, if thou drawest out the arm, touch the head as long as thou knowest the pulse; then sigh the head, and then bind the arm, and close the vein softly; and beware that thou do not wound the artery when thou seest the head swell, for that is the artery: eschew it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If thou seest blood spurting out like the urine of a child, and it is pale and slimy, know that it is not from an artery: haste thee hence, put on thy thumb and linger, then stretch out thy thumb if it does not bleed; bind the arm and leave it still, and do not move the patient; and be wary, and do not move it until it is healed
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it is not stained and it pains, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts because the head is retracting, staunch it without delay.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a handful of mustard seeds, make a poultice of it, and take half and bind it well up to the other side; if there is no bleeding, that is good; but if there is, if as we have said, from powders that stop blood; and the clotting does not suffice in many situations because of the small size of the wound, and the power of the blood.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps to treat the disease of the head below, and of the ribs, because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is useful for the patient to abstain from the nerve that is below, and if it is not too deep, and if he finds the nerve, and it swells, the wound will either be closed, or by chance will not heal; and this nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, it is likely that you must take the blood of the instrument that numbs; and withdraw the nerve from its place.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it is long enough.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, for it attracts blood without pain, and helps the eyes; and it is best to cauterize with the olive flame or the mirtin flame, for these are the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is better to ask a little less violently the first time, and do not grieve if it does not work the first time; and by chance it may happen that it swells up later, which one must not attempt the first time, but it does not grieve anything.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about cautery is that it must only be used to preserve health and avoid diseases to come; and it is best to cauterize on one of the three veins that are or should be: namely, the cephalic, facial, or basilar. It must be performed at the beginning of the prayer while fasting and after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be performed immediately or after two or three hours.</start_of_turn
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood which is administered for maladies has no fixed dose, but when it is necessary for cure or nourishment, at all hours and in all conditions; and it is not permitted to give it to children under twelve years of age, nor to women who are nursing for more than four months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Blood should not be given to those who have passed 60 years of age
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone feels the need for medicine in any way, if it is permitted to administer wine, even if it has caused a slight diarrhea, if there is retained saliva, so that the veins do not draw out the intestines by the abundance of nourishing humors in the principal parts; do not give wine to anyone who is too fat with meat, or drunk, in whatever degree, or suffering from diarrhea; and if one drinks wine after eating, vomiting, and a swollen belly, and many times of vomiting at women, and of childbirth, and of guarding and of fasting, and whatever virtue, or by any weapon or poison; then subtilize the humors, if they are not too thick, by meat, drink, and medicines, if you can; then give warm or cold bath, if nothing else hinders, to subtilize the blood, and keep it from clotting in the veins, up to the navel; as we have said; and keep this work, this penance, and these pleasures, and similar things; and be bound and joyful, and let the physician be higher than you, and wipe his hand twice or thrice, then draw out the thread from the middle; for if it is too tight or loose, it will not be able to correct without; then wipe the area with the hands, until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the physician with a spoonful of old oil, then put his left hand on that vein below the elbow for a moment or two, while he gives the wine; so that the vein does not swell and cause injury.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like cords to the physician, and if some of them are full of windiness, so that when one puts the flame on, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if one opens the vein, the wound is too wide, for this reason one must advise the physicians in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; but if not, one must repeat the process again until the swelling subsides.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is inflamed, and the patient groans, if one leaves it for a little while or two, and does not bind the arm: by chance there will be abscesses of hair; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it is flowing; and if it is slight, or if there is little blood in proportion to what you see, if you are confident in that loss itself with all the flame upright; and do the work deliberately, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.</start_of_turn>
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb inflamed, do not delay in applying pressure to the bleeding; put on a pad of lint soaked in oil, for it softens the course of blood; and with this administer the lint soaked in oil into the wound so that you close the veins, to stop the bleeding; and this will produce a slight tingling and swelling of the limb when it is applied. If you remove it too soon or leave it on too long, it will come apart.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there comes a large abscess that has happened many times, even when the wound is not severe, if you are hasty, and put on the limb a wet sponge and a warm pack, and hold it for an hour; and know that you must do this after the blood has drained from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after a few days, neither black nor green discoloration will result from this; and if you see this, do not put anything else on it, such as aloe or mastic gum dissolved in vinegar, mustard, or anything similar.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is swelling and appearance of blood in the armpit: put your hand there, and if you feel the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave me alone; do not place anything further on that which we have already said, for by chance in court without an artery; but make it thus: apply pressure dry to endure the wound, then treat it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is dark without, if you leave it as long as it is red; and if you see it large, if you leave it as long as it is subtle; and if it is too thick, if you leave it cool.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for the one who is calm and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound larger and the flame bigger; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make it healthier sooner, and must make it healthier by cutting across, not by pricking. And this method of bleeding is useful for the preservation of blood and nerves, and is worth more than the bleeding that comes from a long wound that is not large.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one who has a cold complexion, it is fitting to give lukewarm bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is faint, give blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, give him before the blood lukewarm bread soaked in honey or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pricks with his finger at the blood vessel, after the issue of moisture of blood, then it is commanded that he cough up phlegm, a foul smelling smoke, and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it sees the arm going pale again, and is well another time, if expedient, when it is full of great blood, that it recover itself and recover itself, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has stiffness, if he is well, should wait at least thirteen hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself well in other parts, if he must be well again, should wait at least two days or three days.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.
