For there is blood in the body which is already clotted, and causes fever; if you can remove a great quantity, and expand the opening as much as it bleeds; then that you may reward all the conditions of the blood, and put your hand over the pulse when it is well, that the blood does not come out instead of the flesh, and this often happens when the patient is negligent; and you must not do more than you see the limb slipping, and make the blood reappear the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly; if it is crooked, that you extend the limb as much as possible, because that would be harmful; but leave it as it is until the second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, until the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein is forced out, and put some ointment over it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not restrain me, until the swelling is gone.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to draw out blood a second time, if the same in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is saved in place of the vein of the head for this reason that it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And if the patient’s hand is plunged into hot water, while the blood vessel is red; then bind it moderately, so that the wound opens properly; then draw out the wound, neither too wide nor too long; or make a large perforation, and join it close to the wrist joint; if it is not possible to withdraw it, repeat the immersion in hot water, and allow the blood to clot naturally until enough has formed; and if this is done, do not reinsert the hand into the hot water, for more has been put into it than in the beginning; the blood of this vessel is more valuable than all the other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salivary vein of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver; and this is the method: strain the hand and plunge it into hot water, until the vein bursts if seen; and if the wound opens, and if you grasp it all the way through, grieve nothing; and do not move too much, for the nerves are all loosened of flesh, and then withdraw the hand from the hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not withdraw it again.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as a skilled physician, if you put oil and lint on the wound to stop bleeding, and do this diligently.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of a mouse, and do everything as I have told you regarding the wound.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is worth for all diseases which are sour of the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the knees and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its blood is that when the patient is in acute pain, and froths over the belly as much as possible, and lies down at the joint of the limb; and if the belly is at the ankle, and by lying down on the limb, comes out a quantity of urine; so too with a large or small rain, or at the ankle, that much is worth doing.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you ward off the nerves that are dry, and keep it moist like when you are grasping; and let the flame be gentle.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be moved without pain, if you reset the bone in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient has to urinate the first time, if he begins the second time at a distance, because the urine is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the same with the other limb equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The groin of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its blood is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for blood that has clotted.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient has a wound that opens or breaks open at the ankle, pull out three nails from the foot; for otherwise the vein will not open. And if it opens, do so in all possible ways, both forward and backward; and it is better that you cut it off, for the flesh is soft and the blood will clot at home.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find [something] that will open or drain it, or towards the little toe, and you keep it closed; keep pressure on the wound until you see blood flowing freely, and then remove the dressing and apply pressure; it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of vacuum
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc.ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction that is done with a burn if it is done in two ways: either it is with great heat or with cold; and the suction that is done by burning and extracting blood if it is done in twelve wounds of the flesh, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is at the nape of the neck; and two others on the two shoulders; and the suction from the mouth; and the suction from the two elbows; and the suction on the buttocks; and the suction on the two arms; and the suction on the two legs; and the suction on the two ankles; and the suction does not treat any wound, except for minor blood vessels that are scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not cause any harm, as we do when we make blood from a vein; and it is not recommended except when it is administered, neither with great heat nor with cold, in any disease that comes from repletion, as long as all the flesh is emptied.</start_of_turn>
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of illness compels it, or by custom, if the physician notes a sneeze during the commencement of the month, or at its end, and throughout; for there are some who, when they must sneeze, suffer a heavy head; and there are some who find swelling and redness in their face, and in their head and neck, and black eyes; and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have lost the tongue, and spit blood; and some who dream, and see blood and wounds and death.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is wet and moist, we command the patient to abstain from food for two hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the physician helps with the headache … which comes from the black eyes; and it shall not be used except after the evacuation of all hair; and this vomiting is useful in place of cephalic blood, and is not to be used by those who are of hot complexion or who have a bad temper, because this causes them great discomfort; and for this reason it is not to be used except by those who are suffering from cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if he who is well is made aware of the danger, he must promptly put the ventouse one place further down on account of the fear of danger.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind blowing in the neck is in lieu of the blood of the head and of the basilisk, and for this reason it is worth to extend the thumb, to split the channel of the beard, and to scratch, and to swell; and it must be pressed gently, for if it is held too firmly, it can cause strangulation or stomachache or pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The biting of the wind in the neck is worth the pain of the head, and swelling and vomiting, and strangulation, and toothache; and it is in lieu of the blood of the basilisk; and it must be commanded to the patient to express his hand to put it there, not to cut an artery, and not to vomit blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windsings cause such suffering in the chest as in mouth disease, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in lieu of the ailments of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The biting of the wind in the armpits is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these three veins; and command the patient not to press too deeply, for the skin is sensitive, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is so severe that it causes swelling of the underlying tissue, and diseases of the bones; it is therefore necessary that the suction should be large and strong, and have a good grasp; and in case it should slip, it will cause great damage.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds of the thighs are so painful that they draw blood from all parts of the body, cause ancient pains of the groin, and swelling of the belly and testicles; and lead to the loosening of bones; and are in consequence of these three sophenes and two dislocations, and all these things loosen the body after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction is to put it on empty first, and then gradually add tension, and put it on firmly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the flesh red and swollen, and see the colour of the blood; then let go, and put the suction back on, and take care of the position of the body, for there are some who have a bad temper and are clumsy: if you should only wound once, you will cause great wounds and deep wounds; and do it cautiously.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not large, it can be wounded three times: the first time to open the great vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is not large, it can be wounded three times: the first time to open the great vein. And if its veins swell with blood, it is sufficient to do so once.</start_of_turn>
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins burst with blood, if we renew them often; if they are not expected, if they are fiercely inflamed, and if they are perceived as being perforated, it is fitting for those who have thick skin and hard veins, and who have wide pores, that you apply the leeches of oil aperitif and dissolving: if it is in summer, oil of violet, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seeds; and if it is in winter, oil of cresson, or lilac, or chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, if you take bitter almond oil, or balsamite oil, or oil of angelica, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the patient has soft flesh and large pores, it is not fitting to apply oil, but it is fitting to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or elderberry water, or watermelon juice, or pot liquor, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And whoever has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or vinegar, and sumac, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive discharges should rise from wine strong, or from aquavit of sage, or from decoction of dandelion or chamomile, or from other similar things; and do not cover themselves with a bandage before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the ventosation, and must rise when they are expected to rise and when they are risen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are feverish must keep cold, and if they are too hot and inflamed; if they must take cold things, such as pomegranate seeds and cucumber and lettuce easily, and similar things; and eat meat, barley broth, and moist food.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, if they take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine middle between strong and new, and eat barley porridge, and eat meat and small oilseeds and herbs; and when they will be ventilated, they must drink more than eat; and must give to others no wine before or after, for to comfort the principal members; and be discreet about it, but it must not be that only those who are hot drink it
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and the kidney, and upon the belly and the buttock and the arm and the thigh, for in these members there is no suffering from wounds except for that which is caused by drawing blood from one member to another; and we do this upon the nipples when they do not bleed spontaneously; to remove the viscosity which is in the member, as we do when we apply a bandage to the belly and the buttock to make the member more flexible; and to relieve the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, for by its attractive power it attracts the swelling or dislodges the stone; and thus it makes them rise when we apply it to the liver and the spleen when there is retained congestion. These compresses are administered empty without any liquid, and never together with water that is cold or tepid, except in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the compress with hot water or with water or with herbs that are appropriate for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there are two broad palms and a half of barley, or about a quarter of an inch, as much as to push out an awl; and it should be from flaxseed, so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb; and there should be in the middle a splinter of thorn or iron, to hold the bandage firmly, and there should be large and small ones according to the ailments and the severity of those who take them; for the blisters of the intestines are other than the intestines, and the magras are other than fats.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must put this suction cup on the limb: grasp the bandage firmly or with a dressing, and put it through the splinter which is through the suction cup, so that it sticks neither to the front of the suction cup nor to the patient; and then put it on the limb, and two must be put on the perforation which we have said, so that when we see that it is going well, we can remove the suction cup; and grasp the dressing as before, and do it often, if you are able.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction which is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all its sharpness, neither vein nor opening is to be made, except when it is plain that the disease is acute, and is placed upon the limb only as much as is necessary; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suctions are not to be made except in limbs where it is not possible to place a vacuum due to their small size, such as the liver and the gums, and similar things; and in their nakedness of hair, such as in the groin or navel, and other similar things; and the quality of the patient is such that when we find veins that are in soft, clear veins without any swelling, we must take them; and we put on a little water, until they are full, and do not have anything in their belly; and then either close the vein and the suction, or else wipe the limb until it is red, and put on the veins; and when they are full, and swell, if it is possible to put on the suction, we must do so, for this is worth more afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, if you lift the limb easily, then immediately with a little water, swallow well, and then spit out; and if the limb remains too long after the juice has gone, if you wet a bandage of lint in cold water and put it on, until the swelling has subsided; and if the swelling is great, put on broken glass or splints, or similar things, until it is subsided; or you take out half of the nails from the limb, and leave them until they burn out, if you stop now; if you do more, take other nails.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the nails do not take hold, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you insert a needle until the nails are out, and then put them back, as soon as they feel the blood, if they burn; and when you see that they are bleeding, if you sprinkle on a little aloes and gum arabic, or charcoal, they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is frequently necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear now, dear son, that in this book there is something which no former writer has ever seen, no letter has ever read; and for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never found anything like it. I know of no other way save by the learned books of the ancients, or by studying them and learning them by heart and by experience. And I have set forth in this book what is contained in them, abbreviating it at the end and making clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the two chapters preceding.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book contains the sum of the word and the chapters or the learned men put their understanding into it, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proved to know learn this noble art and learn from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a break or dislocation or twisting or swelling, if you must hasten the recovery of the patient from one side and from the other, if nothing else hinders you, if weakness of the limbs, or youth, or old age, or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and mix cold baths, that is to say cold showers, and oil and vinegar and chamomile, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fatty foods, and do not fill the veins with too much meat, until you are certain that the patient will not suffer from after-pain or swelling of the limb; if the patient recovers before the first treatment has ended, let him rest quietly beforehand.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the bones are broken and begin to heal, if it is known that the patient must not be given meat that causes great swelling, or if there is viscosity, as with flour mixed with water, and rye, and peas, and beans, and fish, and wine, and other things like these.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For part of the swelling subsides when the bone is more solid and the fracture is more stable.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken by fractures and decrepitude do not well resume or knit according to their nature because of the drying up of the limbs; neither those that are too tender, like bones of small children; but there is no cure, leave it resting on the broken bone itself with great tension which has occurred, and join the limb together, as much as it forces; and do not move it at all, for because of this it is necessary to nourish with great meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breakages that go to the marrow, and others by cutting, as with the size of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a breakage with a wound, and a breakage with a small tear.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	When there is stiffness in a limb, it has its own origin and its proper instrument in the restoration; as it is remembered to come in its place; and it is known that the fracture of a bone is recognized by its turning, which is well recognized by its loosening and by pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it may well have twisting, or fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not possible for me to do anything but move the hand, but put on medicines that come after this, and then hold it now discreetly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the wound which bursts forth that is in the armpit, and which are the two parts of the joint, must now be set equally, even as after an incision; and if an incision is made which is too close to the edge, if you leave any hanging, until the incision is healed; then set it equal to the muscle as you can gently and cautiously, and the wound which has burst must be restored more gently than the restoration of these or when there are fragments. Then strain it as you can afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken fragments in the bone, if they are two parts, and it is the hand or the foot, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or two strings, or one string and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb that are broken are loosened, remember with all your might to stabilize the additions to the muscle as you do, and keep that by your work no wound or pain should arise to the patient; and adjust well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the swelling is beautiful, and does not constrain him too much, do not press so much as they do who make it come about by their work at incisions and contractions of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the limb is fixed in place, if the patient keeps it still, neither awake nor asleep, neither turning nor moving in any way; and keep the limb firmly secured so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	When it feels no pain, if it is not firmly fixed, and you must put it in partial use so that it feels no pain; keep it correctly positioned, so that there is no twisting until it is restored; and the degree of damage to the limb is according to what I tell you.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limb is broken in various sizes, shapes and forms.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members such as arms and thighs and the like: if you must cover them with soft and fine cloths; and for those that are large, such as bones and legs: cover them with a wide and strong band, for the large bands embrace the whole great limb and strain it equally, so that there is no tension; then put on firm supports, three tours or four according to the limb, and strain your hand one inch at the circumference, then go up to the fracture and strain less, than the fracture then lets go a little; and soften the limb a little, as long as you take most of the limb back, then take up another band, and strain the dislocation back to its original position; then put back at the bottom of the fracture, and strain moderately, not too strong nor too weak, as we said at the beginning of this chapter; then put between the bands some supports of linen or cloth, so that they are even all around, and then tie everything up securely with your stitches, without any displacement or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is swelling or abscess, put upon something soothing the abscess with heat, which will soften the swelling; and leave it until it subsides. Then strain upon your toes, and let them be half of a large cane resting firmly, or of staff which one makes from sticks, or of rags of wool, and let them be like this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the staff that one puts upon the break be greater and broader than the others; and be as long as it is suitable for the limb in small or great size; then strain upon the toes just as you did at the first hour, and then bind beneath a thread of linen without too much tension; for if the thread is too thick, like those fools who make their threads from hemp fibers, it is a great mistake, for the thread will not be even if it is too fine, and it will not suffice that there be less space between two bones.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is bruised by the threads after the stripping in the flesh, if you put soap on them, I put coarse linen or coarse cloth on them, so that they do not bleed.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a wound-cleaner and the bone is fractured, I will speak of the cure for it later.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And so, if it cannot be forced out by hand, grasp the broken limb first thing.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not permissible to put these stars up except after five days or seven, or more as you deem necessary following an incision. And when this is done, the method of ancient plasters is used to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take flour that adheres to the walls of the mill, mix it with abundant eggs, and make this concoction, not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of plastering that restores fracture in various positions, and it is the same for women and young children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of packing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley, linseed, laurel, asafoetida, gum arabic, mugwort, and mix them with an egg; mix mirra and aloes with a third of an egg; mix alechil with eight eggs; and grind them all together; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this packing, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is useful for torsion: take mugwort and vismut, mix with X parts; myrrh and aloes, mix with seven parts; acacia, mix with six parts; arnica, mix with ten parts. Grind them well and mix with water or eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of immobilizing joints and bones loosened from their sockets, and relieve pain coming from them, and reduce swelling of the bone, and fracture: take new linen, moisten it in oil and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These bandages do not restore me, but they are good to appease post-cautery pain, and bones properly relieve the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other means of supporting that is worth torsion: take dried fig tree leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods of immobilizing involve restoring the fracture of the bone and diminishing the remaining after-effects of the cautery
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of chamomile, chamomile flowers, violets flowers, barley flour, and quince seeds; grind them, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar of coriander or water, and use it
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more violent than the first, when an abscess hardens during restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of gentian, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and chamomile, of each an equal part; and grind, and confect with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two not too soft not too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that we must put something dry and warm on the limb to restore it, such as mirre and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is useful for wound and pain: take mugwort and chopped onions or fennel, and balsam, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of them.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bones are not bruised of their place; if you do not loosen with your hands for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen and oste the displacement now; and take a light bandage, and a wet sponge, and immerse in water, and lift up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased; then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or oil of rose, and bind on a nut, until you are sure of the abscess being gone; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be sure of the pain, then renew the gentle binding, and a little displacement, and do not strain it so much as before; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain, and swelling around a bone, and if the pain persists, you must support and bind it firmly, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not move from the limb anything that we have said, if it does not slip out by itself after three days or four, or five, or seven; do not leave it for twenty days, as one sees, until the bruise has disappeared, and the joint has returned to its place; then restrain it more than before, and swell the flesh, as I said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, do not hesitate but to bathe it with warm water every time you loosen it, and each time cut a little piece of the sinew. By this means the swelling will depart from the limb and restore the member without causing further damage.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many are the ways of fractures, and diverse figures, and the causes are diverse; for there are fractures which are made by percussion of a spear, and the collarbone which is broken throughout its entirety, as is seen in hailstone or dust; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or if the spear pierces the bone from the outside inwards, and is called this kind of fracture "absolue"; and is the wound of these great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fracture or dislocation of the bone, or fracture of the nail or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst fracture, which approaches the gut that is beside the bone, or it is on the bone, and is this wound great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound which is closed in the bone as subtly as a nail, and the fracture is slight, and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by a pierce, or by a splinter, or by a similar thing, and causes the piece of the bone to enter inwards, and is like the swelling which is seen when one boils over pots; if between the teeth.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those who have soft bones, as in children; and in all these kinds of fracture, small pieces are detached if like stars; and I will speak of them later
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all these breaks by the loosening above them, by the incisions of the tents, and by the corrupt flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The like of hair is known by that which when one has discovered the bone, and has wiped over it, if the black break is opened.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s ailments, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, emission of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes watering and reddening, and other similar things in greater or lesser degree, if it does not sense without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any imminent mishap, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling first comes to you, and it is in the armpit, if so, you must remove the bone in front of the wrist from the joint that you must put in place.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you hasten to remove the bone in front of the elbow, so that the bone of the limb is corrupted, then comes the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the breaking of a bone reaches the covering of the brain, if you know how to make the fractured part whole, take hold of the patient's head and uncover the bone in every way possible, and on the wound more heavily than you think; and if blood comes from the uncovering of the bone or from an abscess, if you can, use what is useful and fill the wound with damp cloth soaked in rose oil. Then rest the wound until the abscesses have subsided, and be sure of the bleeding has stopped; then begin to bind up the bone according to two methods: one method if the fracture is close to the heel, and the other if it is far from the heel.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another wound that is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And so if you have various sized swellings, some are thin and others are thick, and they are pointed or iron-like; and on their lower parts, do not touch the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and tough, if you must pierce through, even if you administer swellings with poultices, do not make them go beyond the test of the bone; and must have beneath the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must do this several times, for if pieces of bone come to lie in the place of the thickness of the bone, because of the poultices you must give for the test. And this is the form of the two methods of poultices.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the brittle bone is that you put on one poultice over the bone, and twist your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put on another poultice in another place a little later, and do the same all around; then close the incisions of the space between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you could, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any other instrument that you have like nails, pincers; and keep your hand away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	When you have set the bone firmly and treated it, if you can, reset the fragment that is remaining from the bone to any other instrument resembling a chisel, but make sure it is more tense and subtle than the other chisel; and if nothing remains of the small bones, do not remove any fragments, if the bones are only slightly fractured by some instruments; then close the wound with sutures and dressings as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is like the Galen method, which is more useful; and the load is very strong, and that is his word.</start_of_turn>
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either by fracture or by displacement of muscle, so that when you have uncovered that part, you must place the thumb of your injured finger against the flesh, as it is formed:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not pierce from one side, but from the two costs; if you pierce from the side towards the bone; then make a small mark above, so that you can easily grasp the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below; for if it is near the bone, if the bone is easily moved, because it is well placed, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks but does not pierce the skin, the bone is simply cut through from above; and there are small pieces remaining. If you wish to remove the rough edges, you must have various quantities of the blunt rasp available, so as to smooth each piece according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are before great rasps, and afterwards more subtle, and you do not cease doing this until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and subtle breaks, it is necessary to provide the cause according to its situation; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not thoroughly studied this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the ulcer is discovered, then you must take a bandage of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in oil rose, and put it on the wound; then take another bandage doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and oil rose, and put it on the first bandage; and do this more gently than you wish, that you do not break the ulcer, and give it by mouth another line of medicine, and do not restrain it more than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for one or two days, until the swelling of the wound is calmed, then take it off, and give medicines as above, such as radish root, flour of times, and powdered incense, and an astringent, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and give adequate medicines without biting. And take care that the wound is well closed, that you do not leave it open, nor let it gather pus, for when pus gathers on the linen of the brain, if it is pressed and twisted, it causes great harm to the patient; for when anything biting is put on the ulcer, if it is not done properly by mouth.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed, therefore, if no other mishap befalls the patient, as we have said, if there be doubt concerning it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness does not depart immediately, except for the medicine that has been placed upon it, which has some virtue, if you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drapel, and you put it upon the wound; then you cure it in the manner of cures which are suitable, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then comes the treatment in the manner of cures that it is allowed, as long as it is sane.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, if you can swallow your little toe or pierce the nail without pain, and put the break back into your index finger and at the nail head outwards, until the nail returns to its natural position; do this gently, and keep the patient from feeling pain in your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the limb, and cannot come from below, if you can, put the limb even with the top of a thick stick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, if you do another, and hurry to restore the first joint if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the abscess has subsided, then bathe the head of the nail with attempts to strip the linen, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must break it again somewhere else, if the fracture is there; and be as strong as you can in your attempts to fill the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should mill the tents in the burn, and die each for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not seem to understand that this should be so, but it is fitting that they should be milled in the making of an egg-aubun and powdered spices; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Never put feathers of a goose instead of tents, and if there is any soft drape about, and if you keep the pincer, and blow on the patient among them; or do as you will see.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out while you are working, if you put some lint or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in some linseed oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if after that the abscess does not come out, if you put on pressure by pushing, with flour of flaxseed and powdered incense, confirmed with egg-aubun; then put on soft compresses, and do not bind tightly; and if it breaks without force, and the pieces are small, if the extractor has suitable instruments for this, then cut the opening, and cure the wound with covering material and ointment, as with pressure and medicines suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside, if you cure the tent, and put in flints of lead, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the route of the mandible.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is routed downwards, and there is no wound, and the fracture is only slight, and is not broken thoroughly, except for the curvature inwards, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the outer part, to bite down with the thumb of the affected hand in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take the thumb of the right hand, and grasp the fracture lightly, and hold it apart with the other hand, and keep it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if it is necessary to administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth causes pain, or a fracture, if they are strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put a broken jaw cerate on and put over it a double drape; and put over the drape a large staple well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it to the muscle as you please, and command the patient to rest and eat lean meat.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure is deformed, if the bone is fractured at the third part, and then reset it to its place; then put on a plaster cast, of pounded powder with much egg or oatmeal, after you have set the cerate; and put on the plaster clean linen, and if the plaster is loose, and the patient’s condition does not worsen, leave it as it is until it heals; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the patient has a wound that comes open, if we have already said many times what we have said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, award that no part of the bone is fractured; if slight of the bone has escaped, cover it with something that covers it.
