de la forcele	forcefully</start_of_turn>
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and if it breaks in two manners: when it is broken and loosened in four places, and there are fragments, and that is the lightest to restore; or if there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the break is when the wound faces downwards, take two assistants, so that one holds the limb where the force breaks; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then set the break even, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of lead or linen, and be large as you need; and stretch and hold the forcele, and strain the ball with your hand, so that you set the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to support the head of the shoulder, when it comes out of place, if you must know, the patient lies supine on his belly, and place the shoulder blade between the nipples, and keep the minister there until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris there, if you must know, make an incision there; and force out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join together by any means, if the socket is at one of the incisors you have; but that you place between the shoulder blade and the breast bone this instrument to keep the wound open.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a scoop, but it is not quite so, and let it be as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and there shall be two nails, as you see, and one shall be large, and the other small, as is the curve of the wound that you made when you treated the bone; and when you are assured of the suture, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the suture, if you use a dressing and a bandage, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the afterburn comes, if it is moist, apply oil of roses, rue and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is in pain and swelling, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the fine powder of mill and egg-white, and put on soft stockings, and put a sponge pad below the rump; then take a very large bandage of a palm of width, then put on two layers of dressing on the stockings, and the plaster; then take a subtle splint of three fingers wide and long, and wrap around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage remains fixed; and put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage on the collar, and take off the sponge pad from the painful side, and from the painful side; and leave the dressing part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture steadily, and that you clearly see that the splint does not move from the fractured bone, if the reward comes again, and if the patient remains conscious; and do manage the patient on his back, and put under him a small pillow under the rump, to lift up the limb above; if it will align the fracture by the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it unless it is absolutely necessary, until about twenty days; then repeat the plastering, if you see that there is still need for it, and strain and leave it on, until it is restored; and it is restored in about eight days, and in less time many men recover.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the traction, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it thus until it is restored; and it is restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time to any home.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder blade is broken or displaced from its socket, it must not be forced out by force; if it appears according to the fracture figure, and is restored according to its natural form in all possible ways; then take out the limb powder with abundance of eggshell, and bandage lightly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle splint, wider than the shoulder, and as the splint is fixed firmly in no place of the shoulder, if you use the bandage of flax, so that the splint lies evenly; and then strain it with all your might, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the limb carefully; and every time it softens, if you strain, and put back the splint if it has gone out of place, and leave the patient lying on his side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if the fracture has healed, and be joyful, for it is not the bone that breaks easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and does not yield at all, if it persists, and the bone, make do with the forceps to subdue the abscess at its source.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and does not yield at all, if it persists, and the bone, make do with the forceps to subdue the abscess at its source.</start_of_turn>
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is never broken in a thousand, but it has happened thus; but it often breaks when running away.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in this way, if it declines downwards, and causes the patient great pain, and thirst, and vomiting, and by chance blood spurts from the broken bone, and one feels quite well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that if the patient lies soven on his back, and puts one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae and assemble the ribs of the two costae with your hands, and gently put everything in its place as it should be; then put on bandages and bandage the outside of the bone with fine salt, or some other soft matter, and cover with a cloth, and bind the whole thing around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the patient slowly on his back, and strain gently, and praise for a whole hour when it is loosened, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if it seems to loosen, because of corrosion or because of inflammation that comes from the bone, or pain or swelling, if you are in a hurry, loosen it, and scrape the dressing, and treat what caused the wound; then reinforce the dressing, and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the bones.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Bones that break in the chest do not come forth except after a great swelling behind the back, and at the head downwards; and they do not yield forth except for that which makes them slippery; and one feels them well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is if you put back the fracture equally, as it should be done
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then put on the dressing and bind it with a bandage, if you are able to do so
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the bones is downward towards the belly, if it causes great pain, and swelling, like blood, for the bone points the belly; and there is vomiting, and all together there is great loss of blood, which is a grievous matter, and many have died from it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is said that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push back the wind.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after eating hot food, which is harmful, does not go away.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If it comes, let it be so.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that one should not put compresses on the body to dry it, for this is like reason; however, there is doubt that the compress will not draw out the moisture from the body due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that of nowhere must cover the limb with greasy wool, and put on tenses between the ribs in order to measure equally the hour round, then either cure with the treatment of pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points towards the belly, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is possible to open above the fractured bone, and put in place some instruments to support it; and then you must fracture the bone, treat it gently, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with dressings, until it is healed
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the armpit sweats excessively, put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on gloves; and treat until the limb recovers from the swelling, and keep away from the cost of the wound as much as possible, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden break of bones in the neck, or that it rains; and the same with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	If this happens to anyone, and you know whether it will heal or not, if you take care if you see his hands swollen and limp and dead, and that you cannot move or extend them, and if you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel it

Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is softened on the back and it vomits, it cannot be helped.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Such are mortal wounds: if you do not toil diligently in their cure
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such an accident does not occur, it is the lighter thing.

Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee. de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if there is no sign of improvement even after a long time, and the limb is drooping downwards, and there is pain at the root, and swelling around that which breaks
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above the fracture, until you reach the fracture; and keep the limb in such a way that the fracture is properly aligned; and if the fracture is only at the shoulder, put it in its natural position, until it is perfectly healed
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or is drooping downwards, make the patient sit up on his belly, until the restoration of the fracture is visible.

When you have placed the limb even, if you place upon the socket a peg of wood or bone, and hold the flesh still, if it does not move; then use the hand of the patient to support the cost, as long as the limb is even.

Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If swelling comes, if it does not touch, until the swelling has subsided, and place what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no other mishap; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And thus take two fingers of the hand and grasp the limb above the socket; then hold the patient above a seat; then gently bend the arm over the fist, as far as it can go without causing pain; and put under the fist a cushion or something similar; then put the thumbs of both hands together, so that the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you support the patient on his heel, and bind the arm to his collar, and command two assistants to hold what is above the dislocation with their hands, and the other to hold below all the bones, and stretch the skin to the part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, strain out the spleen and the bowels, and extend the cheshuns of the ministers at their parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the dislocation is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must put one finger in the middle of the elbow and another towards the thumb, holding the shoulder steady; and if the dislocation is towards the thumb, put one finger lightly, with force, until the dislocation is even on both the shoulder and the thumb; then put the dislocation back into place if possible, and hold it steady so that it does not come out again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If the wound comes out again, do not strain for more than three days. Put on a thick bandage of linen and oil of roses until the wound is quiet; then strain, and the way to strain is to put in the dressing under the elbow, then reassemble the arm on the splint, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest; put on the bandage and strain on the splint and the arm, so that the arm is in its place, without anything hindering it, or without breaking the bones.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and put under the bone a splint that is wider and stronger than the others, and have between the splints a space of two finger-widths, so that one splint passes over the elbow two finger-widths beyond the other; then strain on the splints, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see swelling at the elbow and stiffness, as we have said, when restoring the limb after the dislocation, if you doubt the stability, leave it bound until seven days have passed, as we have said; then look for three days whether the swelling has gone down or whether any redness or swelling has appeared in the limb, or whether the limb has become stiff due to excessive stiffness.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If no such accident occurs, if he does not vomit for at least three days or more, and the patient lies down on his back with his hands on his stomach; and put a cushion of wool equal in size under the armpit, and watch for an hour or two to see if the limb is stiff or the ligaments are softened; if the dislocation has been remedied by the power of medicine, and has been given meat as we have mentioned before, in part as before; and when it starts to recover, if it is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the arm and shoulder should be restored in forty days in all cases; and then it must be loosened and bathed and treated with ointments to restore the limb to its proper position
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is painful and emboldened, let it be loosened for a day or two.
de la brisure du bras	And if the fracture of the arm has happened, you must first of all set the limb in its place, and keep it still in this way for as long as necessary; and you must take care that the limb does not move too much, for this would cause more damage.  And you must feed the patient well during this time, and give him medicine for the pain.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of three bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "ulna." One is small and is like a nail that supports the pouch; and the other is large and is like a socket, towards the little finger. By chance the large humerus alone breaks, or the small, and by chance both together break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are fractured, restoration is light, and the healing; but when the great bones are fractured, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they are fractured whole.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is fractured, if it is sufficient to extend it slightly, and put it equal

And if the great bone is fractured, if the limb must be drawn out more strongly; then extend over one cushion, and hold the hand of the patient higher than the other, and the small must be lower than the other two, and let the patient cross his hand over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher than the patient; then extend the limb from the elbow to the wrist, or to the hand, and another limb at the other elbow.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he sets the eye equal, according to its best form.

de la brisure de la main	From the break of the wrist
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the break of the wrist, there are often breaks at the base of the thumb and index finger. It happens often that there is only blood flow left in many cases.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin. de la cuixe brisie	of the broken limb.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz. Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the break is close to the root of the bone, if one of the tendons is towards the point of the break, and the other is towards the outside of the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If it is close to the knee, and then either the tendon is towards the knee, or the collateral ligament; then put the limb parallel to its natural position, and then apply the dressing and bandage, because if it is not done, it will bleed excessively.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a boil above, if you leave it calm and return to your work and your treatment; the dressing is made in a rough manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the break with a strong bandage doubled in two or three places, and to drain the surplus; then rotate the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the limb, below the knee and above the ankle; then rotate the limb and the thigh together with the strong bandage; put on the outer splint and put a splint on the bone of the limb; then put between the limb and the thigh some soft cloth to make them equal in tension; and as you go up the break, and the less you tighten; then take out two threads that you passed between the limb and the thigh, and tie three knots on each side, and keep it like that until the pain is gone; and the swelling, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not make any other dressing or inflammation.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is swelling, if it bursts, and addresses what has come, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them; and if we are unable to do so, it is necessary to cut the limb open, and drain; and cure as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the limb broken in this case when it is set, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration made thereupon, do not be afraid to make the patient suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And if the limb is set in the space of one or two days, or less or more, according to the variety of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of genoil
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hair that grows in the groin often breaks, but it falls out many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If it breaks, if it is not merely a split or a hole, and if there is any wound, pain, or suffering, it is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if restoration is to be made, put the round end back into its place, until it is firmly assembled; then place the plug and insert a round pin, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then restore all the other arrangements that we have mentioned before, such as cautery and the like; if you put into practice each of the precautions that we have mentioned, as long as it is necessary.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if restoration is to be made, put the round end back into its place, until it is firmly assembled; then place the plug and insert a round pin, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then restore all the other arrangements that we have mentioned before, such as cautery and the like; if you put into practice each of the precautions that we have mentioned, as long as it is necessary.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hair that grows in the groin has two roots, for one is called the "muscle" and the other is called the "fleshy part"; and when the latter breaks like that of the arm, restoration is just as it is for the arm, and the work is complete. And if both roots are broken together, if the limb is twisted in every part
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured in two, the limb is twisted forward
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	If the large bone is broken, there is great pain, and it is seen clearly; and it must be sutured
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When thus the limb is brought back, extend it fully and set it straight; bind the joints equally. However, know that if it breaks again it will be more serious, and there will be more pieces; the extension must be less violent and lighter; and be guided by your wisdom.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, if you take .ij. strips of coarse wool that cover the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the knee to the foot; then wrap in .ij. layer of lint from under and over, and bind firmly in the middle; and with this binding the limb will not slip forward or backward, and that is good; and no one should administer any other bandage that is as long as the limb, and if there is swelling, and put the limb in position to prevent movement, and do this at the fracture or wound; and move each joint of the limb to see if there is any displacement or other accident; if there is, cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones that is inside.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in bones that are inside there is no fracture ever and two must be left, and there is only certainty in many situations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in these bones, and you see these bones pressing against each other, if you put so much pain on the limb that it would be as if it were flying towards you, and then put your limb on the ground, where the bones are lifted up, then press the limb until it returns to its place; then put the dressing and bandage on, and put a little bandage under the belly of the limb, and bind the limb steadily, and cover it with a cloth or other things as you deem necessary.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if you loosen the limb, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if you restore them as we have said, do two things with the hand. Then put at the break end a splint of the length of two fingers, and make it wider; then put on the thumb that I have mentioned, and strain it immediately. If there are three or more breaks, break each one and put on at each break an splint according to its quantity, enveloped in a layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the break. Keep the thumb resting on the chief of the thumb over the belly of the thumb as long as it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things I have said concerning other breaks; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the limb is fractured, if you make her sit enlarged, then incline her towards the painful side; and hold her there behind. Then fill the limb of the patient with wool, and put as much inside as I have put; then draw out the patient, and keep her back and front, and then pull out the wool, as much as it comes out of the limb; and bring back the bone with the wool inside; and when she sees her piss, if the bone is still in the wool, and when she has pissed, she will recover. If the fracture is restored, if you see it, take a bladder of barley and bind it to the edge with a bandage, and put the whole bladder in the limb; then blow up the bandage until the bladder is expelled: the limb will then return to its natural position; then fill it with wool and leave it for a few days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or a woman is fractured, if you restore it just as we have said concerning the thigh bone; these fractures are not hidden from the one who studies and uses them, and they are mentioned in my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in many cases the right way of restoration: whether indeed or not you do it.</start_of_turn>
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the groin, when it is broken, take a gooseberry and put it in the groin; then wrap it around with a bandage, and leave it for two or three days, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	From a break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has suffered a fracture with wound, even if it is great, if like the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be sound now, if as we have said the wounds testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, if the vitriol remain, if you have nothing else, then resume the restoration of the fracture in this way, or that, if the pus comes out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus comes out, if you leave the restoration until tomorrow, while the pus is calmed, and do not touch neither a third nor a quarter, for you will risk coming to a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks open is appears above the joint discovered, then you must know that you must hold it firmly in your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to you to hold it equally in your hands, if the handle of this instrument which is of iron, which is three or four fingers long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; for this reason it must be grasped that it grasps three or four fingers, according to what is necessary in the bruise of the wound; and let it be round and have a large head, so that it does not press against the compression on the limb at your work, and be firm before, and large from the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," for it is known that the curved limb must be placed above the head of the visible bone; and when it is once again put together, it must be even so that one side is level with the other.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly hold the bone, you must grasp the head of the bone as long as the instruments have possession of it.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone as we have said, if you have grasped with a curable instrument, such as an incision or hook, at your will; then remove that which remains embedded in the bone, leaving only the rough fragments and small pieces of marrow.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the limb is returned to its place, the patient experiences great pain afterward, swelling that is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then immediately apply a tight black vinegar compress and keep it in place; do not put any cerote or anything else on the wound, as this will cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer oil when you have restored the limb, and leave the wound uncovered, and bind the covering all around, according to the extent of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the breaking; for many times this has happened to fools, and it has caused the patient to die or become lame or corrupt many times; or the inflammation is more mild and painless than the other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the accident has passed, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to set it with sticks; but cover around it, instead of sticks, a firm bandage, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the swelling of the wound has subsided somewhat, if you put oil on the wound that you put on immediately, and you put on healing plasters, as on tetracycline and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it must be that you draw the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is soldered and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it must be that the limb be put back in place gently as if it had never been dislocated
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it recurs, and cannot be soldered but returns to its place, with slight pieces of bone, for it must be that you wish to treat the wound with care, and remove all these detached pieces that cause this pain
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula arises in the limb, or any other kind of corruption, if it is possible, cure it, according to what is said in this chapter above
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and opened on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and others of the great limbs, if you do not treat it, for many times death comes in this case; but leave it alone until it has healed naturally; and if you wish to treat it, do so after twenty days or thirty, and then cure the wound if you wish; or leave it alone.</start_of_turn>
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Hair that comes out from the beard.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Hair that comes out from the beard comes out often after the heat of the bath, even when it is close to the joint, and it is a helpful sign to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot make the limb move naturally.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that it should not slip: if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, make sure that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stiff wine or with much egg or with vinegar; and put them on the wound in bandage, and strain it well, and do not move it from hand to hand until it is healed; and then dislocate it, and do it again, until the nodulation is bony; or you strain on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it can harden all the swellings under the limbs; and if the nodulation has already hardened like stone, it is necessary to break it, if the swelling under the limb is great, and make the excess visible; or do not remove it until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture is restored, and the limb is weak and limp, if there is any fault: because it was too tightly bound and could not be loosened; or because there is too much binding, and it cannot move smoothly; or because of numerous ligatures; or because of too great a movement, not in its entirety; or because there is much blood in the limb, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient move about, and tighten the limb, until the swelling is diminished in him; and give him baths, and make him comfortable and cheerful; then put on a bandage over the limb, so that the bandage will draw out the great swelling, and the blood flows steadily, until the limb is restored to its natural position; and bring back to its usual shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	After the disease, the limb is twisted.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is fractured open, and the limb is deformed, although it has returned to its natural position: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be fractured anew, and many have had this done in our land; this work is blamed, and there follows great evils, and by chance death; although if the swelling and torture are fresh, if one believes they have arisen from warm water, or soft herbs are cooked, like ivy leaves, root, and melilot, and similar things; and it makes one apply a soft dressing, like good aquaintance, and take the nourishment of ivy, and confirm with butter of geline or oil of sesame, and apply the dressing on; or one takes fat figs, and grinds them with horse dung, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone displaced by continuous rubbing and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And keep the limb still at the shoulder joint for an hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron, it is necessary to cover the wound with a bandage, making an incision slightly deeper; and to put padding and a support in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no avail, if you must now restore its place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is left too long, if it swells up, and by chance if it is reset, there will be pain in the limb; for this reason one must not move the limb while it is swollen: many times it brings swelling and other pains; however, when this has happened, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him alone until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and move it gently, and cure each limb as it comes to its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the shoulder to the foot
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The teeth are loosened and the jaws are dislocated in two ways: when they are united by the root of the teeth; or when they are entirely loosened and hang towards the chin, and cause the saliva to flow from the mouth that it cannot hold it, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself several times
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If it is whole and complete, if you must move it, do not touch it; and in such a way that the attendants hold the patient’s head, and look at his pockets from one hand to the other of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two must be loosened, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them in all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And behold the mark be equal, until it returns to its place
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns crooked, even though the two mandibles are together, if they arose from hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are restored equally, and the patient’s mouth is well closed with soft pressure, put upon moist cloths in layers made of rose oil and wax, then bind loosely with fine thread; and let the patient rest on his back, with his arms resting between two cushions, so that he does not move forwards or backwards, neither to the right nor the left, but take moderate food, until the pains are overcome, and keep the jawbone firmly in place.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles do not manage to be put back in their place at a single hour, and are not firmly converted to their roots, if in comes fever and customary nausea, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death is the consequence, in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the snare.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The snare does not know how to unhook from its cost, and is devalued once it is released, and one can feel it.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And if the patient lies sleeping on his back, extend his arms; then press gently at the shoulder joint, and it will return; then put on the bandage and bind it tightly, and hold; the limb which is towards the heel cannot slip away; if not, and if it slips even once, if you re-join the shoulder back in its place, as we have said; then put on the bandage and bind it tightly, and hold, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way bring back the dislocation of the shoulder when it is loosened from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The nails that are loose from the heel must be removed in three ways: first, at the part of the heel towards the ankle; second, at the part of the heel towards the toes; and by chance at the part above the heel, and this is to be expected; do not remove them from behind the heel or from within the nail; and more often than this, remove them from below towards the heel, even among those who have a lot of hair, for at these leaps they are apt to become insane; among those who have enough hair, they leap at the point of pain and return at the point of pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there happens to be a fracture or dislocation, and if the shoulder is bruised with a hard blow, it is dislocated by that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is obvious. You must be certain that the dislocation has been completely remedied; only then should you begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation occurs when it is twisted towards the heel, and distinguishes between the diseased and healthy shoulder, and you will find between their difference a bulge; and at the head of the shoulder you will find a pit, and from the heel to the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an abscess; and the patient will not be able to raise their arm to their shoulder, or move in any way; and also, if it has been dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you will find it immediately on examination; and this method of dislocation must not be used to restore it, when it is new, or when the patient is suffering.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the physician holds the painful limb high up, then puts his thumbs under the armpit, and holds the joint forcefully high up; and the physician holds the limb and stretches it high up, because of this it comes out immediately.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said before, if you must, command the patient to be bathed in warm water; and give them a soft and soothing medicine, such as a decoction of alum, fenugreek and honey in water, or give it directly. Then either keep the patient supine and put under the seat a cushion of linen equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, and put the patient's hand on the cushion, and support the shoulder joint firmly, and treat the hand of the patient; and another attendant holds the chief of the patient's arm, so that it does not move downwards; the shoulder will return at once, and if you see that it remains as you have said: let a person be present who is greater than the patient; and stand on the side of the patient, and stretch the shoulder out from under the patient's arm, and keep the arm high, so that the patient hangs downwards; and another attendant treats the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, if he can hold nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And so we shall do in another way: if the head of the shoulder is loose like a stone in the earth, which is as much as to say that the head is as round as a ball and not too thick or too thin; then let the patient sit with his back straight and his arm hanging down; then stretch out his hand from the other side and the joint will return to its place without difficulty; if it does not return by these means, do this cure: take two fingers of two hands and three fingers wide, and put the thumb over the base of the thumb, following this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie upon the head of the shoulder, draped with a cloth that will not irritate the patient, then put his hands on the patient's buttocks; extend your arms over the patient's long arm, and hold the shoulder at the arm's root, and put your arm on the wrist of the hand, and put the hand on the first space of an elbow of a large size, and extend the lower hands, or leave the forearm hanging down on the other side: the shoulder is now in its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in its place, in whatever way, if you put his buttocks on a sphere of wool equal in size, then put the shoulder pad firmly with a powder of wheat, with incense and balm of egg, on the entire shoulder and around, then strain from the buttocks immediately, and turn the limb over the shoulder, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands immobile.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he keep moving, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal better; and then move more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is firm and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place by moisture or any other cause, if you must, administer cautery three times, as it is put before or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and it lasts for seventeen days, and the dislocation does not hold, and cannot raise the upper arm, then know that the nerves of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the dislocation will never heal in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the elbow, and the arms, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and another support is administered; and it is cured as long as it is sound.</start_of_turn
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And if after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, even though the pain is relieved, it returns to its original state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with the limb, if he wants to see openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is tight, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.
