And it must be known that if it is possible to restore it again as before, when the limb is relaxed, grasp the hand with your two hands and spread the arms apart, and bend the fingers according to the pain of the joint, forward and backward, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and press from the root of the bone that is loosened.</start_of_turn
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not see it return to its place, if you administer strong extension; and if two assistants extend the arm and support it from below, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder joint, and when you have wrapped a double-length and wide bandage around it; and when you look at the joint with the hand, if there is any oil on the joint to soften it, then join the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, put on dry plaster with an egg-shaped weight, and strain the arm, and support the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it for a while, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if you detach the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not hold firmly, recommence the displacement and reattach the limb, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then detach it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, bathe and rub thoroughly, and press until it is eased; or put on the joint a fat sheepskin nail, then leave it in for a night, then take it out and bathe; and when it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the nail back in, and then bathe again; do this two or three times until it is healed. If you see that it has returned to its place, put on a moist poultice soaked in urine and hold it in place; if it returns to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand has loosened, and the return is slight, more so than in other joints, so it must be forcibly returned to its place immediately, while it is still loose, and even if there is swelling or if there is a wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you put the affected limb on a table and extend the limb, and look at it so that it rests equally, then let him put his palm on the surface of the joint and press until it returns normally; it is necessary that you watch to see if it is well placed. Then put the patient’s hand back on the table at the extension and the reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table and the observer place his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, if the strain of the loosening muscles subsides, and you let it resume its place naturally.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not put it back after a few days, the joint will stiffen; and it does no harm to the patient to leave it loose, and he cannot move anything at all: except that the nerves are severed, or the artery; for there is no other reason to extract except by cautery in this case, and by chance there is nothing else
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you place upon the place mentioned above, then strain and leave for five days, then loosen and leave thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not move well, and if there is no pain, if there is warm fluid, and you rub it until it is healed
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the arm bones.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never are the hands desoiled at the wrist part, never at the back of the palm or belly; therefore is the hand stretched out, and the dislocation is held in his pouches until it returns, then the head of the hand is supported and bent towards the part where it is joined; and it is left for two days, and then it is put back in its place; and it is not to be moved, as we have said, until the hand is whole again, and the wound is healed; and do the same if it is desoiled at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is desoiled from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Because of the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the shoulder or the collarbone is loosened, or if there are several dislocations, and there is no remedy, for the patient's life is hurried.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the blood egestions spur in a contrary direction, it cannot be held, and often the limb is softened, or the two thighs or two arms or one. And often the marrow moves at three parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbosite": it is cured if it is known that the gilbosite comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, they say that the old doctors used great words in their cures; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes before the heel, there is no health; and also that which comes directly to the two costae, and one cannot cure it except for that which comes from behind, as I have said; and that the patient should be placed with his face down one inch even, and should have a strain of urine from him, that it does not swell; then I put a cushion under the heel and another at the toes, and I bind the linen around the patient’s ankles, and another at the waist, and I have haunches and calves; and two assistants know the linen, one at the heel and the other at the toes, and they must be well closed, the cushion as we have said, and the patient should put his palms on the spine until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If it does not return by this remedy, take a cube of three fingers in length, and sew the thumb to the side; and let the patient lie on his side, and hold the thumb of the cube to the side, then put the middle of the cube on the spine; and put the thumbs of the two pieces on the other side of the cube, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it is at the root that makes it rotate at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If you see two veins at the root of the patient’s arm of a great length, and two others at the end; and between each vein, sow and sew, a palm’s length; and in each vein one hole, or the knot is corrected, and the veins are firmly bound to the earth so that they do not move; and between two veins are one vein returning, so that the string returns; and there are two minor veins of a palm’s length on either side of the returning string, to bring back the knot; and then bind the string that is between the bones at the knot towards the root, and the other string towards the pieces at the other knot, and the minister binds his knot on the whole string, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, if you put on a dry dressing with plenty of eggshells, and then bind them, and then support it with a tablet of three fingers' length, that will cause the swelling to recede from the rib cage and the upper part of the spine, and then bind with a thread, as we have said; and let the patient take nourishment secretly until he is healed; and if nothing comes to an end of the healing, if you must administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support we have said before; and never give him a piece of lead, and never does it appear behind the shoulder blade, and take care that it is not a dislocation; for it is the bone that has burst, for which we must have no presumption: by chance there will come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocation
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The hip joint and shoulder joint never dislocate except for dislocations alone, never if like other joints; and the joint of the thigh is damaged in three parts: front and back, and front and back; the more inward it is, the more it is damaged in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is this: when you join the painful limb with the tendon, if it is longer, and opens more the patient's knee than the normal, and cannot double his knee at the fire; and it is the thigh that is split open from the heat of the cautery, for which the head of the femur comes loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this displacement is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of this displacement is that if the limb is well placed according to the completion, although it is not doubled at the knee with pain, if one sees that it is done too violently, it cannot be done immediately and is delayed, it retains the urine, swells the belly, and when it walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of that which has behind, if it cannot expand its knee, cannot double, and is that limb shorter than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is displaced from its socket.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If this semblance of dislocation recurs, if it is an old dislocation and does not move according to its setting, if there is no remedy; then I advise you to have suspicion.</start_of_turn>
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you hurry that you return the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for any other remedy.</start_of_turn
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this manner, if you must, appear I with a strong minister, and with two hands hold the limb firmly, or with one that you shall bind upon the knee; and another minister stretches out his hand from under in part as much as he can reach with his hands from his knees to his buttocks, and then he grasps with a loop of thread upon the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend both upwards and downwards together, until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remain suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in three out of four cases. If the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this does not happen, if you must, put a remedy in his appearance. When the dislocation is complete, if you can, lift the patient onto his side, then put the limb on the root of the hip, and the limb which is beside the ankle, then stretch the limb upwards towards the ankle and towards the heel; then take another minister and grasp his arms, and embrace the great limb of the painful hip, and stretch it forward until it returns to its place: if it returns now; for this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not secure it in this manner as we have said, if you know that the two feet of the patient are bound together with a strong thread on the two nails, and on the two knees, and that the limb is extended two fingers more than the others; then suspend the limb from the head of a pole, or upon the ground two arms long; then command one minister to embrace the heel of the ankle, and let another minister stand with the patient, who embraces the ankle, for the joint is now restored.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. Then extend your hands ministers towards him, and watch that the dislocation is even with the hand that is holding it.</start_of_turn>
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.

de la dislocation dou genoil	And if it rests for two or three days, then loosen it and place the bandage upon it; and if you see that they are even, if strained as before, leave them for two days. Then loosen it and make it bleed gently until the limb is comfortable.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint is dislocated in two ways: front to back and front to back; and do not strain it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez. And when it is thoroughly drained, if you make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg under the ankle; then bring your hand to his right hand, and then to his left hand twice, and extend the limb upwards, and hold it firmly; do this twice as we have said, pressing and pulling the limb; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return, make the patient sit on his buttocks on the earth, and put a supporting pillow firmly under his thighs, and cover him with a blanket, so that he does not bleed; then hold the patient’s thigh and one other attendant extend the limb with his hands or by force, as he lies on the neck of the limb; and extend the muscles equally, and tie the bandage either tightly between the patient’s thighs to hold the patient when extending; then put the eyes equally on the dislocation with his hands, and one other attendant holds the limb firmly at the knee, and the dislocation will return immediately.

When it reaches a point, if you put on the dressing and bandage above, and the swelling forms, and you tie the limb to the leg, and keep the nerves above the ankle behind, that the ligature should not be too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling subsides, if the swelling has gone down; then remove the ligature in a third or quarter, and tell the patient for three days. And if it comes before this end, it is not certain that it will not swell again.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	And when they are even, and there is nothing open, if you put some salt on the root of a thistle and hold it against the shoulder for three days, then the strain will subside, and you should leave it for two days, and then remove it; and then rest it until it is healed.</p
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died: if you are not cautious in the cure and do not know how to do it and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and late, do not be ashamed; and start with calming things about the wound, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you remain the limb in its place, even if the wounds remain; and when the limb is in its place, if you administer calming things about the wound, and cure the wound, as it should be, of dried pus; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are fractured, if the bones are displaced, do as we have said in simple illnesses; and keep yourself from going into fear, as I have said, for this will bring you distress according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arm and body.
